10081{_}1012{_}"We heard the firing aloft a moment ago," he said.
10081{_}1013{_}"Did you encounter the enemy?"
10081{_}1014{_}"We were pursued all the way from the German lines," was the reply.
10081{_}1015{_}"Anyone hit?"
10081{_}1016{_}"I think not, though I believe we accounted for one or two of the enemy."
10081{_}1017{_}"Good.
10081{_}1018{_}Will you fly again tonight?"
10081{_}1019{_}"Yes; but not before midnight."
10081{_}1020{_}The French officer withdrew.
10081{_}1021{_}At this one of the aviators raised a hand and the others gathered about him, Frank and Jack with them.
10081{_}1022{_}All wore khaki clothing and their features were concealed by heavy goggles.
10081{_}1023{_}"Careful," whispered the aviator.
10081{_}1024{_}"A false move and we are discovered.
10081{_}1025{_}Spread out now and see what you can learn.
10081{_}1026{_}Gather here at midnight."
10081{_}1027{_}He waved a hand and the Germans, for such Jack and Frank now knew them to be, separated.
10081{_}1028{_}When the two lads were alone a moment later, Jack said:  "Well, this is what I call a piece of nervy business.
10081{_}1029{_}What shall we do?
10081{_}1030{_}Inform the French commander immediately?"
10081{_}1031{_}"No.
10081{_}1032{_}I have a better plan that that.
10081{_}1033{_}They can hardly work any mischief tonight.
10081{_}1034{_}What information they learn will avail them naught for we can warn the French commander later.
10081{_}1035{_}We must find out what they are up to.
10081{_}1036{_}We'll stick close and follow them back to the German lines, if necessary."
10081{_}1037{_}"Good, then!
10081{_}1038{_}Guess we had better do a little skirmishing about.
10081{_}1039{_}It will keep suspicion from us should we be watched."
10081{_}1040{_}"All right," said Frank.
10081{_}1041{_}"Come on."
10081{_}1042{_}CHAPTER VIII  A STARTLING DISCOVERY   With the coming of midnight Frank and Jack returned to the spot where the aeroplanes had been parked.
10081{_}1043{_}Several of the German aviators already had returned.
10081{_}1044{_}The man who appeared to be the leader announced that they would await the arrival of the others before taking to the air.
10081{_}1045{_}The others arrived one at a time until all were present but two.
10081{_}1046{_}The machines were in readiness to ascend the moment the missing men arrived.
10081{_}1047{_}The aviators were at their posts.
10081{_}1048{_}Suddenly there came a shout.
10081{_}1049{_}A moment later the two German aviators who were delaying the departure burst into sight at a dead run.
10081{_}1050{_}"Quick!"
10081{_}1051{_}called one.
10081{_}1052{_}"We are discovered!"
10081{_}1053{_}Immediately the others--Frank and Jack among them--leaped into their machines and soared into the air.
10081{_}1054{_}The last comers also leaped for their craft and succeeded in getting above ground just as rifles began to crack in the French camp.
10081{_}1055{_}Came a sudden cry from the machine nearest that of Frank and Jack.
10081{_}1056{_}The lads saw a man rise to his feet, throw up his arms and pitch, head foremost, toward the ground.
10081{_}1057{_}The aircraft, freed of a guiding hand, rocked a moment crazily and then turned over, hurling its other occupant into space.
10081{_}1058{_}There was a cry of anger from aboard some of the other German craft, but no man raised a hand to stay the flight of his car.
10081{_}1059{_}It would have been suicide and the Germans realized it.
10081{_}1060{_}They sped away into the darkness whence they had come.
10081{_}1061{_}Frank and Jack, in their British hydroplane, went with them.
10081{_}1062{_}For an hour or two the aeroplanes sped through the darkness at undiminished speed; then the foremost craft slowed down.
10081{_}1063{_}The others did likewise.
10081{_}1064{_}"Surely we haven't reached the German lines already?"
10081{_}1065{_}said Jack.
10081{_}1066{_}Frank shrugged his shoulders.
10081{_}1067{_}"You know about as much of what is going on as I do," he returned.
10081{_}1068{_}"Evidently we are going down, however."
10081{_}1069{_}The lad was right.
10081{_}1070{_}The leading German plane swooped toward the earth and the others followed its example.
10081{_}1071{_}A few minutes later all had reached the ground safely and their occupants had alighted.
10081{_}1072{_}The two lads glanced around.
10081{_}1073{_}It was very dark.
10081{_}1074{_}A short distance to the north they could see the broad expanse of the North Sea, stretching away in the night.
10081{_}1075{_}The dark waves lapped the shore gently with a faint thrashing sound.
10081{_}1076{_}The water was very calm.
10081{_}1077{_}Except for the figures that had alighted upon the shore in the darkness there was not a human being in sight.
10081{_}1078{_}To the south, to the east and west stretched miles and miles of sand dunes.
10081{_}1079{_}Just these sand dunes and the waters of the North Sea--there was nothing else in sight.
10081{_}1080{_}At a signal the men gathered around the man who appeared to be the leader.
10081{_}1081{_}Frank and Jack thanked their lucky stars that the night was very dark, for otherwise they would have been in imminent danger of being discovered; and each lad realized that it would go hard with them should their true identities be penetrated.
10081{_}1082{_}The darkness served them like a shield.
10081{_}1083{_}Nevertheless, both lads kept their hands on their revolvers.
10081{_}1084{_}Each had determined that if discovered, he would make an effort to escape in the nearest of the aircraft.
10081{_}1085{_}Each knew that there was little hope of such an escape, but, realizing what was in store for them should they be discovered and captured, they had decided it would be better to die fighting than to be stood up against a wall and shot, or, possibly, hanged.
10081{_}1086{_}The group of men on the bench became silent as the leader addressed them.
10081{_}1087{_}"Men," he said, "it is to be regretted that we have discovered so soon.
10081{_}1088{_}There was still work to be done before the hour for our great effort to crush the British fleet.
10081{_}1089{_}However, to a certain extent we have been successful.
10081{_}1090{_}We have managed to sow the seed of suspicion in the minds of our enemies.
10081{_}1091{_}Prisoners, whom we have allowed to be taken, have let slip words that will lead the British to think our fleet will slip from its base and approach England from the south.
10081{_}1092{_}We know better than that.
10081{_}1093{_}We know that on the night of May 31--which is tomorrow--our fleet will strike the British off Jutland."
10081{_}1094{_}There was a subdued cheer from the assembled Germans.
10081{_}1095{_}The speaker continued:  "Through our efforts the British fleet has been scattered.
10081{_}1096{_}The main portion of the fleet lies to the south and will be unable to reach Jutland in time to save the portion of the British fleet there from destruction.
10081{_}1097{_}Of course, should wind of the move reach the British there would still be time for the fleet to gather.
10081{_}1098{_}But no such word will reach the enemy.
10081{_}1099{_}After sinking the first section of the British fleet, our vessels will steam south and meet the main British fleet.
10081{_}1100{_}The numbers will be nearer equal then.
10081{_}1101{_}We shall be victorious."
10081{_}1102{_}Again there was a subdued cheer, in which Frank and Jack joined for the sake of appearances.
10081{_}1103{_}Again the speaker continued:  "I shall now explain the reason we have landed here.
10081{_}1104{_}Our part in the work has been done.
10081{_}1105{_}Here we shall remain until nightfall tomorrow.
10081{_}1106{_}We shall then sail north and take part in the battle.
10081{_}1107{_}In my pocket here," he tapped the breast of his coat, "are instructions I shall read to you before we leave.
10081{_}1108{_}Until that time we shall rest here, for we have done work enough for the present.
10081{_}1109{_}We shall be safe here.
10081{_}1110{_}Our position now is directly between two French lines and for that reason we shall not be disturbed.
10081{_}1111{_}Of course, if it becomes necessary, we can take to our machines and get out of harm's way.
10081{_}1112{_}We have provisions and water enough to last us; and while the weather is warm, it is still cool enough.
10081{_}1113{_}At any rate, we shall have to make the best of it."
10081{_}1114{_}The man ceased speaking and beckoned the others to follow him.
10081{_}1115{_}He walked a hundred yards to the east.
10081{_}1116{_}There he made a mark in the sand with his foot.
10081{_}1117{_}"Until the time for us to move has come," he said, "let no man set foot beyond that line.
10081{_}1118{_}I make this rule for safety's sake."
10081{_}1119{_}He walked two hundred yards from the sea itself and repeated the operation and instructions; and then to the west.
10081{_}1120{_}"Within these bounds," he said, "we will spend tonight and tomorrow.
10081{_}1121{_}The man who disobeys these instructions shall be shot.
10081{_}1122{_}Do I make myself plain?"
10081{_}1123{_}There was a murmur of assent.
10081{_}1124{_}"Very well," said the leader.
10081{_}1125{_}"Now you are all left to your own devices.
10081{_}1126{_}First, however, I shall pick the watches for the night."
10081{_}1127{_}Frank and Jack, at this, slunk well back into the crowd, for they did not wish to be scrutinized closely.
10081{_}1128{_}But they need have had no fear.
10081{_}1129{_}The leader of the Germans laid a hand on the shoulders of the two men nearest him.
10081{_}1130{_}"You two," he said, "shall stand guard the remainder of the night, one to the southeast and one to the southwest.
10081{_}1131{_}But do not venture beyond the boundaries I have laid down."
10081{_}1132{_}The Germans saluted and moved away.
10081{_}1133{_}The leader moved toward the sea and none of the others followed him.
10081{_}1134{_}Instead, some walked a short distance to the east, others to the south and still others to the west.
10081{_}1135{_}They threw themselves down in the sand.
10081{_}1136{_}A few remained near the airships.
10081{_}1137{_}Frank and Jack walked a short distance toward the sea, but kept some distance behind the German leader, who stood looking off across the water, apparently deep in thought.
10081{_}1138{_}The lads sat down upon the ground.
10081{_}1139{_}"Well," said Frank, "what are we going to do about it?"
10081{_}1140{_}"Do!"
10081{_}1141{_}echoed Jack.
10081{_}1142{_}"Why, there is only one thing we can do--one thing we must do!
10081{_}1143{_}We must get away from here and warn the fleet!"
10081{_}1144{_}"All right," said Frank, "it sounds easy; but how?"
10081{_}1145{_}"Well, that doesn't make any difference.
10081{_}1146{_}We've got to do it."
10081{_}1147{_}"And the moment we have gone our absence will be discovered, the Germans will know the fleet has been warned and the attack will be given up," said Frank.
10081{_}1148{_}"And we don't want anything like that to happen.
10081{_}1149{_}It will be the first time the Germans have mustered up courage enough to come out and give battle.
10081{_}1150{_}We don't want to frighten them off."
10081{_}1151{_}"We don't want to let them sneak up on a part of our fleet unguarded, either," declared Jack.
10081{_}1152{_}"Of course not.
10081{_}1153{_}You say we must give the warning.
10081{_}1154{_}We'll try, of course.
10081{_}1155{_}But first, why not let's put all the aeroplanes except the one we want out of commission?"
10081{_}1156{_}"By Jove!
10081{_}1157{_}a good plan!
10081{_}1158{_}We'll do it."
10081{_}1159{_}"Exactly," said Frank.
10081{_}1160{_}"Then there is still another thing."
10081{_}1161{_}"What is that?"
10081{_}1162{_}"Why, we want the instructions that fellow carries," and Frank waved a hand in the direction of the German leader.
10081{_}1163{_}"He was kind enough to let us know he has them.
10081{_}1164{_}We'll have to take them away from him."
10081{_}1165{_}"Say!"
10081{_}1166{_}exclaimed Jack, "you've laid out quite a job for us, haven't you?"
10081{_}1167{_}"It's got to be done," declared Frank.
10081{_}1168{_}"Well, all right, but we shall have to be careful."
10081{_}1169{_}"Right you are," Frank agreed, "one little slip and the whole thing will be spoiled."
10081{_}1170{_}"Then there must be no slip," said Jack, quietly  "I agree with you there.
10081{_}1171{_}Now the question arise?
10081{_}1172{_}as how the thing may best be done."
10081{_}1173{_}"We'll have to wait until they're all asleep," said Jack.
10081{_}1174{_}"You forget the sentinels won't sleep," said Frank.
10081{_}1175{_}"No, I don't; and they will be the first disposed of.
10081{_}1176{_}They are not looking for enemies from within, you know.
10081{_}1177{_}You walk up to one and I'll walk up to the other.
10081{_}1178{_}We'll be challenged when we get close, of course.
10081{_}1179{_}Then it will be up to us to silence those fellows before they can make an outcry."
10081{_}1180{_}"We'll try it.
10081{_}1181{_}Then what?"
10081{_}1182{_}"Then we'll come back and put the airships out of commission as carefully as possible."
10081{_}1183{_}"That's easy enough.
10081{_}1184{_}All we have to do is to let out the 'gas.'"
10081{_}1185{_}"Next we'll have to go through the commander's pockets without arousing him."
10081{_}1186{_}"That's more difficult, but I suppose it can be done."
10081{_}1187{_}"Next we'll have to get our hydroplane to the water.
10081{_}1188{_}Fortunately, we came down closer to the sea than the others.
10081{_}1189{_}We should be able to do that without awakening the sleepers."
10081{_}1190{_}"Then," said Frank, "we climb in and say goodbye, eh?"
10081{_}1191{_}"That's it."
10081{_}1192{_}"All right.
10081{_}1193{_}We'll work it that way then.
10081{_}1194{_}It's as good as any other.
10081{_}1195{_}Now we'll keep quiet until we are sure everyone is asleep."
10081{_}1196{_}Their plans thus arranged, the lads became quiet.
10081{_}1197{_}They said not a word as they waited for sleep to overcome the Germans, but gazed out quietly over the dark sea.
10081{_}1198{_}CHAPTER IX  THE PLAN WORKS--ALMOST   "Time to get busy."
10081{_}1199{_}It was Frank who spoke.
10081{_}1200{_}All was quiet among the sand dunes.
10081{_}1201{_}The commander of the Germans had laid down upon the ground, some distance from the others, half an hour before.
10081{_}1202{_}Snores from various points announced that most of the men were sleeping soundly.
10081{_}1203{_}Jack and Frank got to their feet  "Careful," said Jack as they separated.
10081{_}1204{_}"Remember, don't give your man a chance to let out a cry."
10081{_}1205{_}Frank nodded in the darkness and walked slowly toward the sentinel he had selected to silence.
10081{_}1206{_}Jack moved in the other direction.
10081{_}1207{_}As Jack came within a few yards of his prey, the man raised his rifle and commanded:  "Halt!"
10081{_}1208{_}"It's all right," said Jack.
10081{_}1209{_}"I couldn't sleep and it was lonesome back there.
10081{_}1210{_}I want company."
10081{_}1211{_}The German lowered his rifle.
10081{_}1212{_}"It's lonesome here, too," he said.
10081{_}1213{_}"Wish you had been selected for my job."
10081{_}1214{_}"I wouldn't have minded it tonight," said Jack, approaching closer.
10081{_}1215{_}The German reached in his pocket and produced a pack of cigarettes.
10081{_}1216{_}He extended the pack to Jack.
10081{_}1217{_}"Have one?"
10081{_}1218{_}he invited.
10081{_}1219{_}Jack accepted a cigarette.
10081{_}1220{_}The German produced a match.
10081{_}1221{_}He laid his rifle upon the ground as he struck the match upon the leg of his trousers.
10081{_}1222{_}It was the moment for which Jack had been waiting.
10081{_}1223{_}Quickly his revolver leaped out.
10081{_}1224{_}In almost the same instant he reversed it and before the German realized what was about to happen he brought the butt down on the man's head with great force.
10081{_}1225{_}The man fell to the ground without a sound.
10081{_}1226{_}Frank, advancing upon the other German, also was challenged when he drew close, but he, too, engaged his prey in conversation.
10081{_}1227{_}As the man turned his head for a moment to gaze across the dark sand, the lad struck him violently over the head with his revolver butt.
10081{_}1228{_}The German dropped like a log.
10081{_}1229{_}A few moments later Frank and Jack met again near the first aeroplane.
10081{_}1230{_}"It'll have to be quick work here," Jack warned "We haven't a whole lot of time, you know."
10081{_}1231{_}Frank nodded that he understood.
10081{_}1232{_}Rapidly they passed from one plane to another letting out the gasoline.
10081{_}1233{_}Five minutes later, with the exception of their hydroplane, which rested some distance away, every craft upon the beach was dry.
10081{_}1234{_}They were absolutely useless--or so the lads thought.
10081{_}1235{_}"Now for the papers," said Jack, as he straightened up after tinkering with the last machine.
10081{_}1236{_}Cautiously the two lads advanced upon the sleeping German.
10081{_}1237{_}Frank raised his revolver and would have brought it down on the man's head had not Jack stayed him with a gesture.
10081{_}1238{_}"No need of that," he said.
10081{_}1239{_}"I don't like to hurt a man except when it is absolutely necessary."
10081{_}1240{_}Frank put the revolver back in his pocket.
10081{_}1241{_}Gently, Jack thrust his hand into the German's pocket.
10081{_}1242{_}He fumbled about a moment and then drew forth a paper.
10081{_}1243{_}Turning his head aside he struck a match and glanced at the paper.
10081{_}1244{_}Then he nodded his satisfaction.
10081{_}1245{_}"This is it," he said.
10081{_}1246{_}Frank, at that moment, had risen to his feet.
10081{_}1247{_}Believing the work was accomplished, he was moving off toward the hydroplane.
10081{_}1248{_}As Jack now made to get to his feet, he chanced to glance at the German he had just relieved of the papers.
10081{_}1249{_}The lad uttered an exclamation of surprise, and no wonder.
10081{_}1250{_}The man's eyes were open and gazed straight at Jack.
10081{_}1251{_}In his hand he held a revolver and it was levelled at Jack's head.
10081{_}1252{_}"Hands up!"
10081{_}1253{_}said the German, quietly.
10081{_}1254{_}There was nothing for Jack to do but obey or be shot.
10081{_}1255{_}His hands went high in the air, but he still retained the valuable papers.
10081{_}1256{_}"Drop those papers," was the next command.
10081{_}1257{_}Jack obeyed and the papers fluttered to his feet.
10081{_}1258{_}The German reached out and picked them up with his left hand while with his right he still covered the lad with his revolver.
10081{_}1259{_}"So you're a spy, eh?"
10081{_}1260{_}said the German.
10081{_}1261{_}Jack made no reply, but a gleam of hope lighted up his eye; for, Frank, chancing to turn for some unexplainable reason, had taken in the situation and was now advancing on tiptoe to his friend's aid.
10081{_}1262{_}"How did you get here?"
10081{_}1263{_}demanded the German, making ready to rise.
10081{_}1264{_}Again Jack made no reply; but none was necessary, for at that moment Frank had come within striking distance.
10081{_}1265{_}His arm rose and fell, and as his revolver butt descended upon the German's head, the latter toppled over in a heap.
10081{_}1266{_}Quickly, Jack stooped and again recovered the papers he had taken so much pains to get.
10081{_}1267{_}"Come on!"
10081{_}1268{_}cried Frank.
10081{_}1269{_}"We haven't time to fool around here.
10081{_}1270{_}The rest of this crowd is likely to wake up in a minute or two."
10081{_}1271{_}Jack followed his friend across the sand.
10081{_}1272{_}They laid hold of the hydroplane and rolled it toward the water.
10081{_}1273{_}In it went with a splash and Frank cried:  "Climb aboard quickly!"
10081{_}1274{_}Jack needed no urging and a moment later the two boys were ready for flight.
10081{_}1275{_}And then, suddenly, there was the crack of a revolver behind them and a bullet flew close to Jack's ear.
10081{_}1276{_}The German leader had recovered consciousness, and springing to his feet, dashed to the water's edge and fired point blank at the machine.
10081{_}1277{_}Fortunately, in his excitement his aim was poor and he missed.
10081{_}1278{_}Before he could fire again, Frank wheeled about and his revolver spoke sharply.
10081{_}1279{_}The German threw up his arms, and with a gasp, pitched headlong into the sea.
10081{_}1280{_}But the sounds of the two shots had aroused the sleeping camp.
10081{_}1281{_}Wild cries came from the shore, followed by heavy footfalls as the Germans rushed toward the water.
10081{_}1282{_}"Hurry, Frank!"
10081{_}1283{_}cried Jack.
10081{_}1284{_}As lightly as a fairy the hydroplane skimmed over the water; then went soaring in the air.
10081{_}1285{_}Frank gave a loud cheer.
10081{_}1286{_}"Safe!"
10081{_}1287{_}he exclaimed.
10081{_}1288{_}But the lad was wrong.
10081{_}1289{_}From on shore came a chorus of angry cries and imprecations.
10081{_}1290{_}Hastily the Germans made a rush for their aeroplanes to give chase.
10081{_}1291{_}None would move.
10081{_}1292{_}Followed more cries and angry shouts.
10081{_}1293{_}"Wait," said one German.
10081{_}1294{_}"I've some gasoline."
10081{_}1295{_}Rapidly he opened up a big can, which he took from the bottom of his machine.
10081{_}1296{_}Quickly the tank was filled and the man climbed into the pilot's seat.
10081{_}1297{_}Another jumped in with him.
10081{_}1298{_}"Give us some of that gasoline!"
10081{_}1299{_}cried another.
10081{_}1300{_}The German shook his head.
10081{_}1301{_}"Not enough," he replied.
10081{_}1302{_}"We'll overtake those fellows and then come back for the rest of you."
10081{_}1303{_}The aeroplane leaped skyward and started in pursuit of Frank and Jack.
10081{_}1304{_}The two boys, believing that they were safe, were going along only at a fair rate of speed when Jack's keen ears caught the sound of the pursuing machine.
10081{_}1305{_}"They're after us, Frank!"
10081{_}1306{_}he called.
10081{_}1307{_}"Impossible!"
10081{_}1308{_}replied Frank.
10081{_}1309{_}"How can they fly without gas?"
10081{_}1310{_}"Well, they're coming, all the same," declared Jack.
10081{_}1311{_}He produced his two revolvers and examined them carefully.
10081{_}1312{_}"You run this thing and I'll do what fighting is necessary," he said.
10081{_}1313{_}"Wish I could shoot like you can; but I can't; and I can't run this machine either."
10081{_}1314{_}The German aeroplane was gaining steadily.
10081{_}1315{_}"He can outrun us," said Frank, quietly.
10081{_}1316{_}"There is only one, thank goodness.
10081{_}1317{_}You'll have to bring him down, Jack."
10081{_}1318{_}"I'll try," was Jack's reply.
10081{_}1319{_}"If I had a rifle I might be able to pick him off now."
10081{_}1320{_}"Well, he won't hardly have any the best of it," said Frank.
10081{_}1321{_}"The chances are he has no rifle either."
10081{_}1322{_}Frank was correct in this surmise.
10081{_}1323{_}Rapidly the German aircraft gained.
10081{_}1324{_}"Crack!"
10081{_}1325{_}the German had fired the first shot.
10081{_}1326{_}It went wild.
10081{_}1327{_}Jack fired, but with no better result.
10081{_}1328{_}"Hit anything?"
10081{_}1329{_}asked Frank, without turning his head.
10081{_}1330{_}"No," said Jack, "but neither did the other fellow."
10081{_}1331{_}"Try it again," said Frank.
10081{_}1332{_}Jack did so; but again the bullet went wild.
10081{_}1333{_}All this time the two craft were flying straight out to sea.
10081{_}1334{_}Once more the German fired and Jack felt something whizz overhead.
10081{_}1335{_}"This is getting too close," the lad muttered to himself.
10081{_}1336{_}Then he called to Frank.
10081{_}1337{_}"Slow down, quick!"
10081{_}1338{_}Frank had no means of telling what plan Jack had in mind, but he did not hesitate.
10081{_}1339{_}The hydroplane slowed down with a jerk.
10081{_}1340{_}The pilot of the German craft was caught off his guard.
10081{_}1341{_}He dashed upon the hydroplane.
10081{_}1342{_}But as he neared it he swerved to the left to avoid a collision.
10081{_}1343{_}It was what Jack had expected.
10081{_}1344{_}Standing up in his precarious position, Jack took a snap shot at the pilot as the German craft swept by.
10081{_}1345{_}At that close distance, in spite of the rate of speed at which the enemy was travelling, a miss was practically impossible.
10081{_}1346{_}The German machine swayed crazily from one side to the other; then dived.
10081{_}1347{_}"I got him, Frank!"
10081{_}1348{_}shouted Jack.
10081{_}1349{_}Both lads gazed over the side at the falling enemy.
10081{_}1350{_}Suddenly the machine righted and descended more slowly.
10081{_}1351{_}"By Jove!
10081{_}1352{_}a cool customer," said Frank.
10081{_}1353{_}"He's regained control of the plane.
10081{_}1354{_}He'll be up again in a moment."
10081{_}1355{_}Again they watched the foe carefully.
10081{_}1356{_}"No, he won't," said Jack, "he's still going down."
10081{_}1357{_}"Then we may as well be moving," said Frank.
10081{_}1358{_}"Hold on!"
10081{_}1359{_}shouted Jack.
10081{_}1360{_}"We can't leave those fellows there.
10081{_}1361{_}They may get to shore or be picked up.
10081{_}1362{_}Then they would give the warning and all our efforts would be for naught."
10081{_}1363{_}"Right," said Frank.
10081{_}1364{_}"We'll go down after them."
10081{_}1365{_}The hydroplane descended slowly.
10081{_}1366{_}CHAPTER X  THE FIGHT ON THE WATER   Below, the fallen aeroplane rested upon the surface of the sea.
10081{_}1367{_}In the darkness, it was hard for the lads to tell just how badly the craft was damaged and whether it would float; but Jack's idea was to be on the safe side.
10081{_}1368{_}While still some distance from the water, there was a shot from below.
10081{_}1369{_}"Hello!"
10081{_}1370{_}said Jack.
10081{_}1371{_}"They're alive and kicking, all right.
10081{_}1372{_}Wonder if we can't go down and get them from the water."
10081{_}1373{_}"It's a better plan, I guess," said Frank.
10081{_}1374{_}"We'll have an even break then.
10081{_}1375{_}This way they have all the advantage."
10081{_}1376{_}He opened up the engine and the hydroplane ran some distance from the position of the men below.
10081{_}1377{_}Then he shut off the motor and allowed the plane to glide down to the sea.
10081{_}1378{_}With the craft riding the swell of the waves, Jack picked up the enemy with his night glass.
10081{_}1379{_}The disabled craft also was riding the waves gently perhaps five hundred yards away.
10081{_}1380{_}Jack gave the position to Frank, and the hydroplane approached the foe slowly.
10081{_}1381{_}Within a range that would make accurate revolver shooting possible, the hydroplane came to a halt.
10081{_}1382{_}As it did so there was the sound of a revolver shot from across the water and something whizzed overhead.
10081{_}1383{_}"Must have some pretty fair shooters over there," said Frank, quietly.
10081{_}1384{_}"However, they can't see us any better than we can see them.
10081{_}1385{_}Of course, they can see our craft all right, the same as we can see theirs, but they can't spot us."
10081{_}1386{_}"No; nor we can't spot them, which makes it worse," said Jack.
10081{_}1387{_}"We'll try a couple of shots for luck," said Frank.
10081{_}1388{_}He raised his revolver and fired quickly twice.
10081{_}1389{_}His efforts were rewarded by a scream, apparently of pain.
10081{_}1390{_}"Must have hit one of them," he said grimly.
10081{_}1391{_}Again a revolver across the water flashed and the two lads heard a bullet whistle by.
10081{_}1392{_}Jack fired but without result and then Frank fired again.
10081{_}1393{_}There was another scream.
10081{_}1394{_}"Either got the other one, or the same one again," said Frank.
10081{_}1395{_}They waited some moments in silence, but no further shots came from the foe.
10081{_}1396{_}"By Jove!"
10081{_}1397{_}said Jack, "you must have got them both.
10081{_}1398{_}Let's go and have a look."
10081{_}1399{_}Slowly, Frank started the hydroplane and they bore down on the enemy.
10081{_}1400{_}Now they were two hundred, then one hundred yards away.
10081{_}1401{_}"Must have got them, all right," said Frank.
10081{_}1402{_}"I----"  The flash of a revolver from the disabled craft interrupted him.
10081{_}1403{_}It was closely followed by another and then two more.
10081{_}1404{_}With a sudden move, Frank changed the course of the hydroplane.
10081{_}1405{_}He felt a sharp pain in his left shoulder.
10081{_}1406{_}"Got me," he called to Jack.
10081{_}1407{_}The latter was alarmed.
10081{_}1408{_}"Where?"
10081{_}1409{_}he demanded.
10081{_}1410{_}"Left shoulder," said Frank, quietly.
10081{_}1411{_}"Nothing serious, though."
10081{_}1412{_}Jack levelled his revolver and fired rapidly at the enemy.
10081{_}1413{_}His pains were rewarded by howls of derision.
10081{_}1414{_}"They tricked us, all right," said Jack, as he reloaded.
10081{_}1415{_}"That's what they did.
10081{_}1416{_}I should have known better, too.
10081{_}1417{_}They almost settled us."
10081{_}1418{_}"We've got to get them, some way," declared Jack.
10081{_}1419{_}"Show me how, and I'll go along with you," declared Frank.
10081{_}1420{_}"Well, I've got a scheme, but I don't know whether it will work or not."
10081{_}1421{_}"Let's hear it."
10081{_}1422{_}"All right.
10081{_}1423{_}But first, can you manage this plane all right with that bad shoulder?"
10081{_}1424{_}"Sure; it's not very bad."
10081{_}1425{_}"All right then.
10081{_}1426{_}Well, you keep under cover about here, moving about just enough to spoil the aim of the foe.
10081{_}1427{_}I'll drop over the side and swim to the enemy.
10081{_}1428{_}I can get there unobserved, all right, because they won't be expecting me.
10081{_}1429{_}I'll pull one of them over and settle with him first.
10081{_}1430{_}Then I'll get the other."
10081{_}1431{_}"I don't know," Frank considered the plan.
10081{_}1432{_}"I suppose it might work, but there is nothing sure about it."
10081{_}1433{_}"There's nothing sure about anything," declared Jack.
10081{_}1434{_}"But it's better than staying here all the rest of the night.
10081{_}1435{_}Besides, we must hurry, you know."
10081{_}1436{_}"That's right," agreed Frank.
10081{_}1437{_}"All right, then.
10081{_}1438{_}So be it.
10081{_}1439{_}Will you take your gun?"
10081{_}1440{_}"No use," said Jack.
10081{_}1441{_}"It would be wet by the time I got there.
10081{_}1442{_}Here I go."
10081{_}1443{_}"Good luck," Frank called after him.
10081{_}1444{_}Gently, Jack lowered himself over the side of the hydroplane, first divesting himself of his coat and shoes; then struck out for the disabled aeroplane.
10081{_}1445{_}Slowly the lad swam, for he did not wish to betray his coming by the sound of a splash.
10081{_}1446{_}The distance was not great and a powerful swimmer, such as Jack, could cover it easily in a few moments.
10081{_}1447{_}Jack did not approach the enemy craft from the front.
10081{_}1448{_}Giving it a wide berth, he swam around it and then, turning quickly, bore down upon the aeroplane more swiftly.
10081{_}1449{_}He swam with his head barely above the water, and he was ready to dive immediately should he be sighted.
10081{_}1450{_}There was not a sound aboard the aeroplane as Jack drew close to it.
10081{_}1451{_}Raising his head slightly, he could see no human form.
10081{_}1452{_}"Funny," the lad muttered to himself.
10081{_}1453{_}"Wonder where they keep themselves.
10081{_}1454{_}No wonder we couldn't hit them."
10081{_}1455{_}He was within a few feet of the disabled craft and he now rose higher in the water to get a good look about.
10081{_}1456{_}Still he saw no one.
10081{_}1457{_}Twice around the machine the lad swam and not a human being did he see.
10081{_}1458{_}"There is something awfully queer about this," he told himself.
10081{_}1459{_}"I'll go aboard."
10081{_}1460{_}He laid hands on the aeroplane and scrambled aboard.
10081{_}1461{_}Quickly he sprang to his feet, ready to tackle any foe that might have seen him crawl aboard.
10081{_}1462{_}Nothing happened.
10081{_}1463{_}Jack made a careful inspection of the disabled plane.
10081{_}1464{_}Then, as he still gazed around, a sudden thought struck him.
10081{_}1465{_}Without taking time to consider it, he sprang suddenly to the side of the plane and leaped into the water and with swift and powerful strokes struck out for his own craft.
10081{_}1466{_}Jack had hit upon the solution of the desertion of the German aeroplane.
10081{_}1467{_}Even as Jack had lowered himself from the hydroplane and swam across the water, the Germans in the other craft had done the same thing.
10081{_}1468{_}Both sides had struck the same plan almost simultaneously.
10081{_}1469{_}Jack, in making a wide detour as he approached the foes' machine, must have passed the two Germans in the water.
10081{_}1470{_}Now, realizing that the Germans must be close to the hydroplane, had they not already reached it, and remembering that Frank was wounded, Jack felt a sudden dread steal over him.
10081{_}1471{_}His long, powerful strokes sent him through the water at great speed.
10081{_}1472{_}But the Germans had not made their presence known to Frank yet.
10081{_}1473{_}Neither was as swift a swimmer as Jack, and for that reason, their progress through the water had been considerably slower.
10081{_}1474{_}Also they had gone very cautiously.
10081{_}1475{_}A short distance from the hydroplane, one had swum to one side of the plane and the second to the other.
10081{_}1476{_}The Germans also had discarded their revolvers, for they had realized they would be useless after their trip through the water.
10081{_}1477{_}Also, not being expert swimmers, they had wanted to be unhampered by weight as much as possible.
10081{_}1478{_}Frank was still guiding the plane about occasionally to avoid a chance bullet from the enemy, but at the moment the Germans came close, he had stopped the craft and was peering into the darkness, straining his ears for the sound of a struggle that would tell him Jack was engaged with the enemy.
10081{_}1479{_}Suddenly a sound came to his ears from across the water, but it was not what he expected, although it was in Jack's voice:  "Frank!
10081{_}1480{_}Look out!
10081{_}1481{_}They are after you!"
10081{_}1482{_}Instantly, the lad understood the situation.
10081{_}1483{_}He drew his revolver with his uninjured arm and sprang to one side of the aeroplane.
10081{_}1484{_}As he did so, a figure reached up and grabbed him by the hand so that he could not fire.
10081{_}1485{_}At the same time a second figure clambered aboard the craft from the opposite side.
10081{_}1486{_}Frank raised a cry:  "Hurry, Jack!"
10081{_}1487{_}Jack needed no urging.
10081{_}1488{_}He was swimming through the water as fast as possible.
10081{_}1489{_}With a sudden move, Frank jerked his hand loose from the grip that held him and turned just in time to encounter the second German.
10081{_}1490{_}Frank raised his revolver and fired quickly; but the German ducked, and before Frank could fire again, he had come up close to Frank and grappled with him.
10081{_}1491{_}In vain Frank sought to release his arm so that he could bring the weapon down on his opponent's head.
10081{_}1492{_}The man clung tightly.
10081{_}1493{_}A sudden lurching of the hydroplane told Frank that the second German was coming aboard.
10081{_}1494{_}Unmindful of his wounded shoulder, Frank struggled on.
10081{_}1495{_}With a sharp kick of his right foot he succeeded in knocking the first German's legs from beneath him; and again the lad tried to raise his revolver to shoot the second German, who now advanced.
10081{_}1496{_}But the latter was too quick for him.
10081{_}1497{_}Closing with the lad, the man knocked the revolver from the boy's hand with a quick blow.
10081{_}1498{_}The weapon spun into the sea.
10081{_}1499{_}The first German returned to the attack.
10081{_}1500{_}"Get him quick!"
10081{_}1501{_}he shouted.
10081{_}1502{_}"There is another one around here some place."
10081{_}1503{_}Jack, at this moment, was within a few yards of the boat.
10081{_}1504{_}"You bet there is!"
10081{_}1505{_}he said between his teeth.
10081{_}1506{_}"And he'll be there in a minute."
10081{_}1507{_}He did not call encouragement to Frank, for he wished to get aboard the plane, if possible, before the men could stay him.
10081{_}1508{_}The two Germans rushed Frank simultaneously, and bore him back in the plane.
10081{_}1509{_}At the same instant, Jack, unmindful of danger that might lurk aboard and thinking only of Frank's danger, laid hold of the plane and climbed aboard.
10081{_}1510{_}Then he stood erect and shouted:  "Come on, you cowards!
10081{_}1511{_}Here's the other one!"
10081{_}1512{_}CHAPTER XI  DAWN--AND A NEW ENEMY   The two Germans, just about to throw Frank overboard, turned quickly at the sound of this new voice.
10081{_}1513{_}They wasted no time.
10081{_}1514{_}"At him!"
10081{_}1515{_}cried one, and leaped.
10081{_}1516{_}The other sprang after him.
10081{_}1517{_}Jack, with his feet wide apart and arms extended, braced himself to receive the shock; and when it came he was ready.
10081{_}1518{_}Frank, in the meantime, sank down in the plane almost unconscious, for one of the Germans had all but choked the life from him.
10081{_}1519{_}As the first German sprang, Jack met him with a straight right hand blow to the face and the man reeled back.
10081{_}1520{_}The second, seeing the fate of his companion, dived for Jack's legs and seized them, pulling the lad down.
10081{_}1521{_}Jack felt out with his left hand and encircled the German's neck.
10081{_}1522{_}Then he squeezed.
10081{_}1523{_}The German gasped for breath as his wind was shut off.
10081{_}1524{_}His hand searched his belt and presently flashed aloft with a knife.
10081{_}1525{_}Jack saw it.
10081{_}1526{_}Releasing his hold on the man's throat, he seized the knife arm with his left hand and twisted sharply, at the same time driving his right fist into the man's face.
10081{_}1527{_}There was a sharp snap and a cry of pain.
10081{_}1528{_}The knife fell clattering to the deck of the plane.
10081{_}1529{_}Jack, very angry, rose to his feet, stooped over, and picking up the German as though he had been a child, heaved him overboard.
10081{_}1530{_}"So much for you!"
10081{_}1531{_}he muttered.
10081{_}1532{_}He stepped across the body of the second German to Frank's side and stooped over him.
10081{_}1533{_}Gently he raised his chum's head to his knee.
10081{_}1534{_}Frank's eyelids flickered and directly he opened his eyes.
10081{_}1535{_}"How do you feel, old man?"
10081{_}1536{_}asked Jack.
10081{_}1537{_}Frank struggled free from his chum's grip and sat up.
10081{_}1538{_}He shook his head once or twice and then rose to his feet.
10081{_}1539{_}"I'll be all right in--Look out!"
10081{_}1540{_}he broke off suddenly.
10081{_}1541{_}He dodged.
10081{_}1542{_}But Jack, not realizing the import of Frank's words, remained still.
10081{_}1543{_}He felt something hot sear the lobe of his ear.
10081{_}1544{_}Wheeling abruptly, the lad saw the German whom he had first knocked unconscious facing him with levelled revolver--the weapon was Jack's own, which he had left behind when he swam to the enemy's aeroplane.
10081{_}1545{_}The German faced him with a smile.
10081{_}1546{_}"Hands up!"
10081{_}1547{_}he commanded.
10081{_}1548{_}But Jack, with a few drops of blood trickling from his ear, suddenly became very angry.
10081{_}1549{_}He objected to being shot at from behind.
10081{_}1550{_}"Put down that gun!"
10081{_}1551{_}he commanded in a cold voice.
10081{_}1552{_}"Put it down before I kill you!"
10081{_}1553{_}The German was struck by the menace in the lad's tones, and for a moment he hesitated and the revolver wavered.
10081{_}1554{_}Then he braced and brought the weapon up again.
10081{_}1555{_}But that moment of hesitation decided the issue.
10081{_}1556{_}In spite of the fact that the revolver was pointed right at him, and that only a few feet away, Jack took a quick step forward.
10081{_}1557{_}The German fired.
10081{_}1558{_}Jack swerved a trifle.
10081{_}1559{_}The bullet plowed through the sleeve of his shirt and touched the skin; but that was all.
10081{_}1560{_}Again the man's hand tightened on the trigger, but he never fired again.
10081{_}1561{_}Jack's powerful left hand seized his wrist and twisted the revolver from it Then, still grasping the wrist, the lad wheeled on his heel.
10081{_}1562{_}The German left the spot where he had been standing as though pulled by a locomotive.
10081{_}1563{_}He was lifted high in the air and, as Jack gave a jerk and then released his hold, the man went sailing through the air and dropped into the sea with a loud splash.
10081{_}1564{_}And at the same moment the intense darkness was shattered.
10081{_}1565{_}The first faint streak of dawn showed in the east.
10081{_}1566{_}Jack sat down.
10081{_}1567{_}Frank did likewise.
10081{_}1568{_}"That settles that," said Jack, briefly.
10081{_}1569{_}"Now we had better get away from here.
10081{_}1570{_}We haven't any too much time."
10081{_}1571{_}Frank, without a word, took his place at the wheel.
10081{_}1572{_}"Feel fit?"
10081{_}1573{_}asked Jack.
10081{_}1574{_}Frank nodded, though he felt terribly faint.
10081{_}1575{_}"Sure you can make it?"
10081{_}1576{_}Jack continued.
10081{_}1577{_}"Yes," replied Frank.
10081{_}1578{_}"Well, I just wanted to know," said Jack, "because here comes a German torpedo boat."
10081{_}1579{_}Frank was startled.
10081{_}1580{_}He turned in his seat, and there, not a mile and a half away, was a ship of war.
10081{_}1581{_}She was flying the German flag and was making directly for the spot where the British hydroplane rested.
10081{_}1582{_}"By George!
10081{_}1583{_}Won't we ever get out of this?"
10081{_}1584{_}the lad muttered.
10081{_}1585{_}"We won't unless you hurry," said Jack.
10081{_}1586{_}"But those two Germans.
10081{_}1587{_}Won't they be picked up and give the alarm?"
10081{_}1588{_}"One of 'em won't," said Jack, grimly, "and I feel pretty safe about the other, too.
10081{_}1589{_}Let's get up in the air."
10081{_}1590{_}Frank tinkered with the motor and took a firm grip on the wheel.
10081{_}1591{_}But the hydroplane did not move.
10081{_}1592{_}"Something wrong," said Frank, quietly.
10081{_}1593{_}"What?"
10081{_}1594{_}demanded Jack.
10081{_}1595{_}"Something wrong with the motor.
10081{_}1596{_}It won't work."
10081{_}1597{_}Frank had bent over and was examining it carefully.
10081{_}1598{_}Came a shot from the German torpedo boat.
10081{_}1599{_}"If we don't get out of here pretty quick," said Jack, quietly, "we won't get out at all."
10081{_}1600{_}Frank made no reply, but continued to tinker with the engine.
10081{_}1601{_}A second shot from the German torpedo boat.
10081{_}1602{_}It skimmed the water ahead of the hydroplane.
10081{_}1603{_}Jack gazed toward the vessel.
10081{_}1604{_}As he did so a small boat put off from the German and headed toward them.
10081{_}1605{_}"They're coming after us, Frank," said Jack, "a whole boatload of 'em.
10081{_}1606{_}How long will it take you to fix that thing?"
10081{_}1607{_}Frank uttered an exclamation of satisfaction.
10081{_}1608{_}"I've found it," he cried.
10081{_}1609{_}"Five minutes," he answered Jack's question.
10081{_}1610{_}"Five minutes is liable to be too late," returned Jack, measuring the distance to the rapidly approaching German boat with his eye.
10081{_}1611{_}"However, hurry as much as you can."
10081{_}1612{_}Frank did not take his eye from his engine.
10081{_}1613{_}"How far away?"
10081{_}1614{_}he asked as he worked.
10081{_}1615{_}"Three quarters of a mile," replied Jack, calmly.
10081{_}1616{_}"Lots of time for us, then," said Frank, still working as swiftly as possible.
10081{_}1617{_}"Maybe," replied his chum.
10081{_}1618{_}"Don't forget they carry pretty fair rifles with them."
10081{_}1619{_}"If we can get started before they shoot, I'll guarantee they don't get us," returned Frank.
10081{_}1620{_}"Well, they'll get us if you keep talking and don't get a move on there," said Jack.
10081{_}1621{_}"They're coming like the wind."
10081{_}1622{_}"That's just the way I'm working.
10081{_}1623{_}She's almost fixed row.
10081{_}1624{_}Can you hold them off?"
10081{_}1625{_}"What, with a single revolver against a score of rifles?
10081{_}1626{_}Not much.
10081{_}1627{_}They're right on us now.
10081{_}1628{_}How's that engine?"
10081{_}1629{_}"Fixed!"
10081{_}1630{_}cried Frank at that moment, straightening up.
10081{_}1631{_}"All right.
10081{_}1632{_}Let her go then," said Jack, calmly.
10081{_}1633{_}"They don't know yet that we're going to run.
10081{_}1634{_}They have made no preparations to fire.
10081{_}1635{_}Evidently they think we shall wait for them."
10081{_}1636{_}Even while Jack was speaking, the hydroplane began to move slowly over the surface of the water.
10081{_}1637{_}Very slowly it went at first, then faster and faster.
10081{_}1638{_}"Halt!"
10081{_}1639{_}came a cry from the German boat.
10081{_}1640{_}Jack picked up his cap and waved it at the Germans.
10081{_}1641{_}"Some other time," he called back.
10081{_}1642{_}"We're terrible busy today.
10081{_}1643{_}Goodbye."
10081{_}1644{_}The German officer gave a sharp command.
10081{_}1645{_}Several sailors sprang to their feet and blazed away at the hydroplane with their rifles.
10081{_}1646{_}Bullets flew by on all sides, but none struck home.
10081{_}1647{_}Again Jack waved his cap.
10081{_}1648{_}"Very bad shooting," he remarked.
10081{_}1649{_}"Looks like some of my--Hello!
10081{_}1650{_}That wasn't so bad."
10081{_}1651{_}For the lad's cap, which he had been waving in derision at the pursuing foe, was suddenly carried from his hand by a German bullet.
10081{_}1652{_}"By Jove!"
10081{_}1653{_}said Jack, quietly, "I wouldn't have lost that cap----" He gazed at it as it floated in the water.
10081{_}1654{_}And at that instant Frank sent the hydroplane soaring into the air with a lurch.
10081{_}1655{_}Jack glanced down into the water.
10081{_}1656{_}"Hold on, Frank!"
10081{_}1657{_}he cried.
10081{_}1658{_}In response to this command, Frank slowed down.
10081{_}1659{_}"What's the matter now?"
10081{_}1660{_}he demanded.
10081{_}1661{_}"Why, one of our erstwhile German friends has come to life.
10081{_}1662{_}He was just about to lay hold of us when you came up in the air.
10081{_}1663{_}Great Scott!
10081{_}1664{_}What do you think of that?"
10081{_}1665{_}"What do I think of what?"
10081{_}1666{_}"Why, the Germans in the boat have just shot him."
10081{_}1667{_}"Shot whom?
10081{_}1668{_}The German?"
10081{_}1669{_}"Yes; they saw him coming after us and evidently thought he was a friend of ours.
10081{_}1670{_}Poor fellow!
10081{_}1671{_}To be shot down by one of his own countrymen.
10081{_}1672{_}And so goes the last chance the Germans had of learning that we have discovered their plans."
10081{_}1673{_}"Then it is a good thing for us they shot him."
10081{_}1674{_}"For us, yes.
10081{_}1675{_}But think of the irony of it!"
10081{_}1676{_}"Well," said Frank, "I wouldn't like to have shot him, defenseless as he was; and I didn't want you to.
10081{_}1677{_}That's why I didn't suggest having a look for him before we came up."
10081{_}1678{_}"I couldn't have done it," returned Jack.
10081{_}1679{_}"No; nor I; and yet duty would have demanded it.
10081{_}1680{_}For with him alive, there always remained a chance that he would give the warning."
10081{_}1681{_}"It just goes to show," said Jack, slowly, "that even fate sometimes works on the side of the right."
10081{_}1682{_}"True."
10081{_}1683{_}Unconsciously, Frank had allowed the speed of the hydroplane to diminish during this conversation, and the crew of the German boat again had found themselves within range.
10081{_}1684{_}They had started to abandon the chase when the plane soared aloft, but when it had slowed down, they had resumed the pursuit, hoping that something had gone wrong with the craft.
10081{_}1685{_}Several bullets flew about the machine.
10081{_}1686{_}"Great Scott!
10081{_}1687{_}They're at it again!"
10081{_}1688{_}cried Jack.
10081{_}1689{_}"Let's get away from here right now."
10081{_}1690{_}"All right, here she goes," said Frank.
10081{_}1691{_}"Full speed ahead!"
10081{_}1692{_}CHAPTER XII  THE BOYS GIVE THE WARNING   One other adventure, it transpired, was to befall Frank and Jack before they found themselves once more aboard the British battleship, _Queen Mary_; and while it did not result seriously, both lads once more approached the very door of death.
10081{_}1693{_}The morning sun was well above the horizon when Jack, shading his eyes, made out in the distance a smudge of smoke.
10081{_}1694{_}"Smoke ahead, Frank," he called.
10081{_}1695{_}"Hope it's the _Queen Mary_" replied the lad.
10081{_}1696{_}"It should be if I have calculated correctly."
10081{_}1697{_}A few moments later the outline of a large ship of war loomed up ahead.
10081{_}1698{_}"Can you make her out yet?"
10081{_}1699{_}asked Jack.
10081{_}1700{_}"No; but she's built like the _Queen Mary_"  The hydroplane sped on.
10081{_}1701{_}"By Jove!
10081{_}1702{_}She is the _Queen Mary_" cried Frank, a few moments later.
10081{_}1703{_}"We're in luck."
10081{_}1704{_}Frank was right.
10081{_}1705{_}As the hydroplane drew nearer it was plain to make out that the vessel was the giant battleship the lads had quitted the day before.
10081{_}1706{_}"Wonder what Captain Raleigh will think of our information?"
10081{_}1707{_}said Frank, with a chuckle.
10081{_}1708{_}"Don't know.
10081{_}1709{_}We've been pretty fortunate, though.
10081{_}1710{_}I hope we are in time."
10081{_}1711{_}"So do I.
10081{_}1712{_}The trouble is, our ships are scattered so far apart that they may not be able to assemble quick enough in sufficient strength to beat off the enemy."
10081{_}1713{_}"Don't worry; they won't get very far," said Jack, confidently.
10081{_}1714{_}"Oh, I know that.
10081{_}1715{_}But if they should happen to come upon a small portion of our fleet we are likely to get the worst of it."
10081{_}1716{_}"Well, there is no reason why they should be able to do that now.
10081{_}1717{_}We know their plans."
10081{_}1718{_}"That's true, too.
10081{_}1719{_}And they won't, unless it is decided to engage them in spite of their numbers, trusting reinforcements will arrive in time."
10081{_}1720{_}And, though the lad had no idea he was making a prophecy, that is just what actually occurred.
10081{_}1721{_}The hydroplane now was less than a quarter of a mile from the _Queen Mary_ and Frank reduced its speed abruptly.
10081{_}1722{_}Whether this sudden slowing down had anything to do with what followed it is hard to tell; but, no sooner had Frank reduced the speed of the craft, than the plane wabbled crazily.
10081{_}1723{_}"Look out, Jack!"
10081{_}1724{_}shouted Frank.
10081{_}1725{_}"She's going down!"
10081{_}1726{_}Jack had not realized that there was anything wrong and now he did not grasp the full significance of Frank's words.
10081{_}1727{_}What Jack thought Frank meant was that he was going to glide down to the deck of the battleship.
10081{_}1728{_}Frank, however, knew that there was something seriously wrong with the craft.
10081{_}1729{_}His first thought had been to jump after crying out to Jack, but seeing that his friend had not understood, Frank stuck to his post, trying as well as he knew how to bring the plane to the sea as gently as possible.
10081{_}1730{_}For a moment it seemed that he would succeed, for, as it neared the water, the plane righted itself.
10081{_}1731{_}Frank drew a breath of relief.
10081{_}1732{_}But his relief was short-lived.
10081{_}1733{_}After remaining upon a level keel for one single instant, the hydroplane turned turtle.
10081{_}1734{_}There came a cry of warning from aboard the _Queen Mary_, and even before the falling boys struck water, boats were lowered over the side, manned, and dashed to the rescue.
10081{_}1735{_}Although Frank had been unable to maintain the plane on an even keel, his efforts had done some good; for the distance was not so great from the water when the plane capsized as it would have been but for his strenuous efforts.
10081{_}1736{_}Jack uttered a cry of alarm as he felt himself being hurled into space, for he had not realized what was about to happen.
10081{_}1737{_}Frank, on the other hand, had realized his position full well and no sound escaped him as he was thrown into the water.
10081{_}1738{_}In falling, Jack was thrown clear of the machine, which struck the water with a great splash.
10081{_}1739{_}Not so Frank, who, held in by the wheel, was carried down with the plane.
10081{_}1740{_}The lad was very close to death at that moment and he knew it.
10081{_}1741{_}He had caught a deep breath as he was drawn under, however, and this stood him in good stead.
10081{_}1742{_}Calmly the lad reached for the large pocketknife he always carried, and with this, under water as he was, proceeded quietly to cut the sides of the craft sufficiently to allow him to escape.
10081{_}1743{_}And in this he was successful.
10081{_}1744{_}At last he was free and struck upward as swiftly as possible.
10081{_}1745{_}When it seemed that his lungs must burst for want of air, his head suddenly bobbed upon the surface.
10081{_}1746{_}He gasped as he inhaled great breaths of the fresh air.
10081{_}1747{_}A boat approached at that moment and he was drawn aboard, where he sank down.
10081{_}1748{_}Jack, when he came up from below, had thought first of Frank.
10081{_}1749{_}Rapidly he scanned the surface of the sea for some sign of his chum or of the wreckage.
10081{_}1750{_}Seeing neither, he knew what had happened.
10081{_}1751{_}Taking a deep breath he dived.
10081{_}1752{_}It took the lad some time to locate the sinking mass of wreckage below and when he did come upon it there was no sign of Frank.
10081{_}1753{_}Jack stayed below until he could stand it no more; then rose to the surface.
10081{_}1754{_}There rough hands seized him and dragged him into a boat.
10081{_}1755{_}In vain the lad struggled.
10081{_}1756{_}He wanted to get loose so he could make another attempt to rescue his friend.
10081{_}1757{_}"Frank!"
10081{_}1758{_}he cried.
10081{_}1759{_}"Be still," said a voice kindly.
10081{_}1760{_}"Frank is safe in the next boat."
10081{_}1761{_}Jack uttered an exclamation of relief and lay still, resting from his exertions.
10081{_}1762{_}And so they came again to the _Queen Mary_ and were lifted aboard.
10081{_}1763{_}Frank and Jack clasped hands when they stood on deck and Jack exclaimed:  "By Jove!
10081{_}1764{_}I thought it was all over when I couldn't find you down there."
10081{_}1765{_}"I thought it was all over myself for a minute," said Frank.
10081{_}1766{_}"That's one time when this old knife of mine helped out.
10081{_}1767{_}I brought it back with me."
10081{_}1768{_}He displayed the knife and patted it affectionately.
10081{_}1769{_}"How do you feel?"
10081{_}1770{_}asked Jack.
10081{_}1771{_}"First rate.
10081{_}1772{_}And you?"
10081{_}1773{_}"Fine.
10081{_}1774{_}Now we want to see Captain Raleigh."
10081{_}1775{_}At this moment the third officer approached.
10081{_}1776{_}"Captain Raleigh will receive you the moment you have put on some dry clothes," said the third officer.
10081{_}1777{_}"But we must see him at once," exclaimed Frank.
10081{_}1778{_}"Change your clothes first," said the third officer kindly.
10081{_}1779{_}"But----" Frank began.
10081{_}1780{_}"I have Captain Raleigh's orders for you to report to him the moment you have changed," said the third officer sharply.
10081{_}1781{_}"You will hurry, if you please."
10081{_}1782{_}Frank could see that there was no use protesting further.
10081{_}1783{_}He shrugged his shoulders and the two boys made their way to their cabin.
10081{_}1784{_}"The big chump," said Frank, as he slipped off his wet clothing.
10081{_}1785{_}"The whole British navy might be sent to the bottom while we are doing this.
10081{_}1786{_}What are a few wet clothes?"
10081{_}1787{_}"I guess it was the way we went at it," said Jack.
10081{_}1788{_}"If we had blurted out what we knew----"  "To tell the truth, I've a good notion to say nothing about what I learned," said Frank.
10081{_}1789{_}Jack looked at his companion in the greatest surprise.
10081{_}1790{_}"Oh, no, you've not," he said at last, as he slipped on a dry shirt.
10081{_}1791{_}"Don't you believe I haven't," declared Frank.
10081{_}1792{_}"I'm mad.
10081{_}1793{_}I don't like that way of doing things.
10081{_}1794{_}Now if it had been Lord Hastings----"  "Well, it wasn't," said Jack.
10081{_}1795{_}"I'm afraid that's one trouble with us."
10081{_}1796{_}"What do you mean by that?"
10081{_}1797{_}"Why, simply that he allowed us to get too familiar with him.
10081{_}1798{_}The result is we expect it from others, and when they don't treat us that way we are disappointed."
10081{_}1799{_}"That may be it, of course," Frank conceded.
10081{_}1800{_}"But at the same time, I didn't like the tone of the third officer just now."
10081{_}1801{_}"Perhaps I didn't either," said Jack, "but I've got more sense than to show it.
10081{_}1802{_}As a matter of fact, I suppose we should have obeyed without question."
10081{_}1803{_}Frank continued to mumble as he slipped into a dry coat.
10081{_}1804{_}He picked up his cap and moved toward the door.
10081{_}1805{_}"Ready?"
10081{_}1806{_}he asked of Jack.
10081{_}1807{_}"Almost.
10081{_}1808{_}How's that shoulder?"
10081{_}1809{_}"All right.
10081{_}1810{_}How's your wound?"
10081{_}1811{_}"Just a scratch.
10081{_}1812{_}Didn't even bleed much."
10081{_}1813{_}Jack picked up his cap and also moved toward the door of the cabin.
10081{_}1814{_}"Guess maybe he'll let us see Captain Raleigh now," he said.
10081{_}1815{_}"Come on."
10081{_}1816{_}Frank followed his chum.
10081{_}1817{_}On deck almost the first person they encountered was the third officer.
10081{_}1818{_}"Didn't take you long," he said with a smile.
10081{_}1819{_}"That is because we have important news," said Frank.
10081{_}1820{_}"Come, then.
10081{_}1821{_}I'll conduct you to the captain myself," said the third officer.
10081{_}1822{_}Frank and Jack hurried after him.
10081{_}1823{_}Captain Raleigh greeted the two lads with a smile, as they stood at attention before him.
10081{_}1824{_}"You are back really sooner than I expected you," he said quietly.
10081{_}1825{_}"Have you learned anything?"
10081{_}1826{_}"If you please, sir," said Jack, "I shall skip the details until later.
10081{_}1827{_}The German high sea fleet will be off the coast of Denmark before midnight!"
10081{_}1828{_}"What's that you say?"
10081{_}1829{_}he demanded.
10081{_}1830{_}"It's true, sir," replied Frank, quietly, stepping forward.
10081{_}1831{_}"The German high sea fleet, in almost full strength, will attack our patrol squadron in the Skagerak, off Jutland, tonight!"
10081{_}1832{_}For one moment Captain Raleigh looked at both lads closely.
10081{_}1833{_}Then he cried sharply, including all in the cabin with his words:  "Follow me!"
10081{_}1834{_}He sprang for the bridge!
10081{_}1835{_}CHAPTER XIII  PREPARING FOR BATTLE   "Eleven o'clock!"
10081{_}1836{_}Jack returned his watch to his pocket.
10081{_}1837{_}"Not much time to gather the fleet together," he said quietly to Frank.
10081{_}1838{_}"No," was his chum's reply, "but you can rest assured that all can be done will be done."
10081{_}1839{_}Captain Raleigh, upon the bridge, had issued orders swiftly.
10081{_}1840{_}The _Queen Mary_, which had been heading southward after Frank and Jack returned aboard, was quickly brought about.
10081{_}1841{_}After several sharp commands to his officers, Captain Raleigh motioned to Frank and Jack.
10081{_}1842{_}"Come with me," he said.
10081{_}1843{_}"You shall tell me what you have learned as we go along."
10081{_}1844{_}The two lads followed him.
10081{_}1845{_}Straight to the wireless room went the commander of the _Queen Mary_.
10081{_}1846{_}"Get the _Lion_ quickly," he ordered the wireless operator.
10081{_}1847{_}"_Lion!
10081{_}1848{_}Lion_!"
10081{_}1849{_}the call went across the water.
10081{_}1850{_}There was no reply.
10081{_}1851{_}"Try the _Indefatigable_," was the next command.
10081{_}1852{_}"_Indefatigable!
10081{_}1853{_}Indefatigable_!"
10081{_}1854{_}flashed the wireless.
10081{_}1855{_}The receiving apparatus aboard the _Queen Mary_ clicked sharply.
10081{_}1856{_}"_Indefatigable_ answering, sir," reported the operator.
10081{_}1857{_}"Send this," ordered Captain Raleigh, and passed a slip of paper on which he had scribbled rapidly to the wireless operator.
10081{_}1858{_}The message read as follows:  "German high sea fleet to attack off Jutland tonight.
10081{_}1859{_}Inform Admiral Beatty.
10081{_}1860{_}Relay message.
10081{_}1861{_}Am steaming for Danish coast to engage enemy.
10081{_}1862{_}Information authentic.
10081{_}1863{_}Follow me!
10081{_}1864{_}(Signed) "RALEIGH."
10081{_}1865{_}A short pause and again the receiving apparatus on the _Queen Mary_ clicked sharply.
10081{_}1866{_}"O.K., sir," said the operator.
10081{_}1867{_}"All right," this from Captain Raleigh.
10081{_}1868{_}"Call the _Invincible._"  Again the wireless began to click.
10081{_}1869{_}Two minutes later the operator reported:  "_Invincible_ answering, sir."
10081{_}1870{_}"Send the same message," instructed Captain Raleigh.
10081{_}1871{_}It might be well to state here that all these messages were sent in code, for it was probable that a German vessel of some sort might be within the wireless zone and, if able to read the messages as they flashed across the sea, would have communicated with the main German fleet.
10081{_}1872{_}One after another now the wireless of the _Queen Mary_ picked up the battle cruisers _Defense, Black Prince, Warrior_ and the super-dreadnaught _War-spite,_ all of which chanced to be within range of the _Queen Mary's_ wireless.
10081{_}1873{_}The destroyers _Tipperary, Turbulent_ and _Nestore_ also answered the call and were instructed to proceed to the Skagerak at full speed.
10081{_}1874{_}And to each vessel, as it answered, the single word "relay" was flashed.
10081{_}1875{_}This meant that Captain Raleigh wanted the word sent to other vessels of the British fleet not within her own wireless radius.
10081{_}1876{_}And the answer to this was invariably the same:  "O.K.!"
10081{_}1877{_}Still in the wireless room, Captain Raleigh turned to Frank and Jack and said:  "Now, I shall be glad to know how you boys learned this information."
10081{_}1878{_}Jack explained as briefly as possible.
10081{_}1879{_}Captain Raleigh interrupted occasionally as Jack proceeded with his story and when the lad had concluded, he said quietly:  "You have done well, young sirs.
10081{_}1880{_}England has much to thank you for."
10081{_}1881{_}"But will the others arrive in time, sir?"
10081{_}1882{_}asked Frank, anxiously.
10081{_}1883{_}"That," said Captain Raleigh, "I cannot say.
10081{_}1884{_}You may be sure that they will come to our assistance at all possible speed, however."
10081{_}1885{_}"But you will not await them there, sir?"
10081{_}1886{_}"No; I shall engage the enemy single handed if necessary."
10081{_}1887{_}With this Captain Raleigh turned on his heel and would have left the wireless room.
10081{_}1888{_}At that moment, however, the wireless began to click again, and the commander of the _Queen Mary_ paused.
10081{_}1889{_}"For us?"
10081{_}1890{_}he asked.
10081{_}1891{_}The operator nodded.
10081{_}1892{_}"Admiral Beatty, aboard the _Lion_, calling, sir."
10081{_}1893{_}"Take his message!"
10081{_}1894{_}There was silence for a moment, and then the operator called off the clicks of his apparatus.
10081{_}1895{_}"Admiral Beatty wants to know your source of information," he reported.
10081{_}1896{_}Captain Raleigh dictated a reply.
10081{_}1897{_}Again silence for a few moments; and then the operator said:  "The _Queen Mary_ is ordered to the Skagerak under full speed.
10081{_}1898{_}Hold the enemy until the arrival of the main fleet.
10081{_}1899{_}Assistance on the way.
10081{_}1900{_}_Indefatigable, Defense_ and _Black Prince_ also steaming for Jutland to lend a hand.
10081{_}1901{_}Open the engagement immediately you sight the enemy."
10081{_}1902{_}"Sign O.K.," said Captain Raleigh.
10081{_}1903{_}The operator obeyed and heard the operator aboard the _Lion_ repeat his message.
10081{_}1904{_}"I guess that is about all we can do," said Captain Raleigh.
10081{_}1905{_}Again he turned to leave the room and once more paused at the door.
10081{_}1906{_}"Keep your instrument going," he ordered the operator.
10081{_}1907{_}"Pick up any ship that may not have heard the message.
10081{_}1908{_}Come, boys," this last to Frank and Jack.
10081{_}1909{_}The boys followed their commander back to the bridge; thence to his cabin.
10081{_}1910{_}The interchange of messages had taken time, and glancing at his watch now, Frank saw that it was after one o'clock.
10081{_}1911{_}"Great Scott!"
10081{_}1912{_}he exclaimed.
10081{_}1913{_}"I had no idea we had been in the wireless room so long."
10081{_}1914{_}Back in his cabin, Captain Raleigh seemed to have forgotten the boys' presence.
10081{_}1915{_}He was busy for perhaps an hour poring over a mass of charts and other papers.
10081{_}1916{_}Frank and Jack stood at attention.
10081{_}1917{_}They were becoming uneasy, when Captain Raleigh looked up suddenly.
10081{_}1918{_}"Pass the word for the first officer," he instructed.
10081{_}1919{_}Jack sprang to obey and in a moment the first officer of the _Queen Mary_ was in the cabin.
10081{_}1920{_}"Shape your course for Jutland proper," ordered Captain Raleigh.
10081{_}1921{_}The first officer saluted and obeyed.
10081{_}1922{_}"We'll go back to the wireless room," Captain Raleigh informed the two lads.
10081{_}1923{_}"I want to keep you boys near me for I may desire to ask a question at any moment."
10081{_}1924{_}The lads followed their commander back to the wireless room.
10081{_}1925{_}"Any calls?"
10081{_}1926{_}he asked the operator.
10081{_}1927{_}"One coming now, sir."
10081{_}1928{_}"Repeat it as it comes."
10081{_}1929{_}"Very well, sir.
10081{_}1930{_}_Indefatigable_ calling."
10081{_}1931{_}"Ask her position."
10081{_}1932{_}"Five miles south by southwest, sir."
10081{_}1933{_}"Inform Captain Reynolds that we shall slow down and wait for him to come up with us."
10081{_}1934{_}"Very well, sir."
10081{_}1935{_}The operator sent the message.
10081{_}1936{_}"O.K., sir, signed, 'Reynolds,'" the operator reported a few moments later.
10081{_}1937{_}"Ask her if she has picked up any other vessels."
10081{_}1938{_}"Destroyers _Fortune_ and _Shark_, sir," reported the operator a little later.
10081{_}1939{_}"Good.
10081{_}1940{_}Give Captain Reynolds our position and tell him to keep working his wireless.
10081{_}1941{_}Tell him we are likely to need every ship we can bring up."
10081{_}1942{_}"Very well, sir."
10081{_}1943{_}The operator sent the message.
10081{_}1944{_}"O.K., again, sir," he reported.
10081{_}1945{_}Captain Raleigh passed a slip of paper to the operator.
10081{_}1946{_}"On this," he said, "are enumerated the ships that should be somewhere in these waters.
10081{_}1947{_}Pick up as many of them as you can.
10081{_}1948{_}As you give the warnings when answered check them off on the list.
10081{_}1949{_}If any information is asked, call me."
10081{_}1950{_}"Very well, sir," replied the operator, taking the slip of paper.
10081{_}1951{_}"No other instructions, sir?"
10081{_}1952{_}"No.
10081{_}1953{_}Send the same message as you sent to the _Indefatigable_."
10081{_}1954{_}Captain Raleigh motioned Frank and Jack to follow him and left the room.
10081{_}1955{_}"I want you two to attend me closely," he informed the lads.
10081{_}1956{_}"I shall have lots of leg work that must be done from now until we sight the enemy and even after that.
10081{_}1957{_}You shall act as my orderlies tonight and while the battle lasts."
10081{_}1958{_}Frank and Jack were considerably flattered by this.
10081{_}1959{_}They knew that Captain Raleigh had been pleased with their work.
10081{_}1960{_}They saluted.
10081{_}1961{_}"Very well, sir," they exclaimed in a single breath.
10081{_}1962{_}"I want one of you to report to the wireless room, room, ready to bring me any message that may come," instructed Captain Raleigh.
10081{_}1963{_}"The other will stay here.
10081{_}1964{_}You can suit yourselves about your positions."
10081{_}1965{_}"I'll go to the wireless room, then, sir," said Frank.
10081{_}1966{_}"Very well.
10081{_}1967{_}Report to me instantly a message is received."
10081{_}1968{_}Frank saluted and took his departure.
10081{_}1969{_}Jack stood at attention in Captain Raleigh's cabin as the commander of the _Queen Mary_ again plunged into a mass of charts.
10081{_}1970{_}Captain Raleigh sprang to his feet and opened his watch.
10081{_}1971{_}"Four o'clock," he said.
10081{_}1972{_}"We won't reach Skagerak until well after six.
10081{_}1973{_}I am in hopes the Germans will not try to pass through before early morning.
10081{_}1974{_}We shall be ready for them then."
10081{_}1975{_}"How big a fleet have we there now, sir?"
10081{_}1976{_}asked Jack.
10081{_}1977{_}"None, to speak of.
10081{_}1978{_}Two or three cruisers and a couple of torpedo boats.
10081{_}1979{_}I believe we have a submarine or two there also, though I cannot be sure of that."
10081{_}1980{_}"We'll lick 'em, sir," said Jack, enthusiastically.
10081{_}1981{_}Captain Raleigh smiled.
10081{_}1982{_}"I hope so," he said quietly.
10081{_}1983{_}At that moment the first officer called from the bridge.
10081{_}1984{_}"Battleship overhauling us fast, sir."
10081{_}1985{_}"Probably the _Indefatigable_," said Captain Raleigh.
10081{_}1986{_}He went on deck.
10081{_}1987{_}Jack followed him.
10081{_}1988{_}CHAPTER XIV  CHANGED ORDERS   At the same moment Frank came running up.
10081{_}1989{_}"_Indefatigable_ reports she has sighted us, sir!"
10081{_}1990{_}"Good!"
10081{_}1991{_}exclaimed Captain Raleigh.
10081{_}1992{_}"I felt sure it was the _Indefatigable_.
10081{_}1993{_}Tell her we shall steam slowly until she comes up with us."
10081{_}1994{_}Frank saluted and returned to the wireless room.
10081{_}1995{_}Now Captain Raleigh gave an order to the first officer.
10081{_}1996{_}"Have all hands piped to quarters, Mr.
10081{_}1997{_}MacDonald."
10081{_}1998{_}Instantly, all became bustle aboard the _Queen Mary._ Men rushed hither and thither; but in a moment order was restored out of the seeming confusion.
10081{_}1999{_}Followed by Jack, his first and second officers, Captain Raleigh made an inspection of the giant battleship.
10081{_}2000{_}He addressed the different groups of men as he passed and told them what was about to transpire.
10081{_}2001{_}"It is likely to be a one-sided battle at first," he told the men quietly, "but I know that none of you will shrink because of that.
10081{_}2002{_}You have fought against odds before now.
10081{_}2003{_}You will not mind doing it again."
10081{_}2004{_}The men cheered him.
10081{_}2005{_}His tour of inspection completed, Captain Raleigh ordered:  "Let each man be served with a good meal and let them have two hours sleep--all but the watches."
10081{_}2006{_}The necessary orders were given and a short time later the men were eating heartily.
10081{_}2007{_}Then they went to their quarters, where some lay down to sleep while others sat in groups and discussed the impending battle.
10081{_}2008{_}Shortly after five o'clock Frank and Jack found themselves alone in their cabin, having been relieved of duty for an hour.
10081{_}2009{_}"It's going to be a great fight, Frank," declared Jack.
10081{_}2010{_}"You bet it is.
10081{_}2011{_}It will be the greatest naval battle of history, if the bulk of the British fleet comes up in time.
10081{_}2012{_}Never before has such a vast array of giant fighting ships as will be engaged in this struggle contended for supremacy.
10081{_}2013{_}In total tonnage engaged and in the matter of armament and complement it will outrival even the victory of Nelson at Trafalgar and the defeat of the Spanish Armada.
10081{_}2014{_}And the British, as always, will win."
10081{_}2015{_}"Let us hope so.
10081{_}2016{_}But, as you and I know, the Germans are no mean opponents.
10081{_}2017{_}Considering the fact that, since the outbreak of the war, they have had little opportunity to practise war tactics on the sea and practically no chance at all to practise gunnery, the few battles that have been fought have proven them foemen worthy of the best we have to offer."
10081{_}2018{_}"True," said Frank.
10081{_}2019{_}"Until reinforcements arrive they will outnumber us.
10081{_}2020{_}I don't know how many to one."
10081{_}2021{_}"To my mind it is foolish to engage the German fleet with only a few ships," said Jack.
10081{_}2022{_}"It won't gain us anything.
10081{_}2023{_}I believe we should retreat slowly and draw them on."
10081{_}2024{_}"I believe that would be a much better plan.
10081{_}2025{_}We might engage them at long range, running slowly before them.
10081{_}2026{_}Then, when the main fleet came up, we would take them by surprise."
10081{_}2027{_}And even at that moment the same plan was being revolved in the mind of Vice-Admiral Beatty as, in his flagship, the _Lion_, he steamed swiftly northward.
10081{_}2028{_}By this time the battleship _Indefatigable_ had drawn up almost on even terms with the _Queen Mary._ The wireless of both ships were busy as the commanders exchanged greetings and discussed their plans for battle.
10081{_}2029{_}A little later, as the _Indefatigable_ drew even closer, Captain Reynolds of the _Indefatigable_ flashed this message:  "I am coming aboard you."
10081{_}2030{_}Half an hour later he came over the side of the _Queen Mary_ and disappeared with Captain Raleigh in the latter's cabin.
10081{_}2031{_}Directly an aide was despatched for Frank and Jack, who made their way to their commander's quarters.
10081{_}2032{_}"So!"
10081{_}2033{_}exclaimed Captain Reynolds, when his eye fell on Jack, "this lad is one of the two who gained this important information, eh?
10081{_}2034{_}Let me hear your story again, sir."
10081{_}2035{_}Jack repeated the account of the adventures he and his friend had had the night before.
10081{_}2036{_}Captain Raleigh produced the paper the lads had taken from the commander of the German air squadron and the two commanders scanned it together.
10081{_}2037{_}"Well, there is one thing in our favor," said Captain Reynolds.
10081{_}2038{_}"The Germans will fail to get the air support they are expecting."
10081{_}2039{_}"There probably will be other aircraft with the fleet," said Captain Raleigh.
10081{_}2040{_}"Most likely.
10081{_}2041{_}Probably a Zeppelin or two with them.
10081{_}2042{_}Fortunate we have these new anti-aircraft guns aboard.
10081{_}2043{_}They weren't completed any too soon.
10081{_}2044{_}Raleigh, what ships are in the Skagerak now?"
10081{_}2045{_}"Only three, I believe.
10081{_}2046{_}The _Glasgow, Albert_ and the _Victoria_, the former a battle cruiser and the latter two torpedo boats.
10081{_}2047{_}If we can arrive in time there will be five of us.
10081{_}2048{_}Then, if the _Warspite_, the _Invincible_ and the cruisers _Defense, Black Prince_ and _Warrior_ come up in time we will be more on even terms."
10081{_}2049{_}"Exactly.
10081{_}2050{_}But the main fleet, farther south, will hardly arrive in time I am afraid; and, by the way, you are wrong in your calculations.
10081{_}2051{_}The _Warspite_ is with the main fleet."
10081{_}2052{_}"Is that so?
10081{_}2053{_}So, then, is the _Edinsburgh_, the _Tiger_, the _Peerless_, the _Terror_, the _George IV_ and the _Richard_?"
10081{_}2054{_}"Yes; those, with a dozen battle cruisers and a score of torpedo boats, comprise the main fleet.
10081{_}2055{_}If they arrive in time, the Germans must either run or be sent to the bottom."
10081{_}2056{_}At this moment a message was handed to Captain Raleigh from the wireless room.
10081{_}2057{_}"Change in orders," said the commander briefly, after scanning the piece of paper.
10081{_}2058{_}"We are to engage the enemy at long range and seek to draw him farther into the North Sea.
10081{_}2059{_}Orders have been sent to the three ships off Jutland to fall back before the approach of the enemy until we can join them, if they sight the enemy before we arrive.
10081{_}2060{_}If not, we are all to retire slowly.
10081{_}2061{_}The _Invincible_, three cruisers and half a dozen torpedo boats will join us soon after dawn.
10081{_}2062{_}The main fleet cannot arrive until two hours before noon."
10081{_}2063{_}"By Jove, Raleigh!"
10081{_}2064{_}exclaimed Captain Reynolds, "I am better satisfied with those orders.
10081{_}2065{_}There is more chance of success now.
10081{_}2066{_}It would have been foolhardy for us to engage the whole German fleet."
10081{_}2067{_}"I agree with you."
10081{_}2068{_}"Well, I'll get back to my vessel now."
10081{_}2069{_}Captain Reynolds arose and extended his hand to his fellow commander.
10081{_}2070{_}"In case----" he said simply.
10081{_}2071{_}Captain Raleigh gripped the hand.
10081{_}2072{_}Then he accompanied Captain Reynolds and saw him over the side.
10081{_}2073{_}It was now after 6 o'clock.
10081{_}2074{_}The German fleet was due off Jutland at almost any moment.
10081{_}2075{_}Captain Raleigh and Jack made their way to the wireless room.
10081{_}2076{_}"Get the _Glasgow_," commanded Captain Raleigh of the operator.
10081{_}2077{_}"_Glasgow!
10081{_}2078{_}Glasgow_!"
10081{_}2079{_}went the call.
10081{_}2080{_}"_Glasgow!_" came the reply a few moments later.
10081{_}2081{_}This conversation between the two commanders ensued:  "Have you sighted the enemy?"
10081{_}2082{_}This from the _Queen Mary_.
10081{_}2083{_}"No," from the _Glasgow_.
10081{_}2084{_}"Have any of your consorts picked up the foe?"
10081{_}2085{_}"Not yet."
10081{_}2086{_}"You received my earlier instructions?"
10081{_}2087{_}"Yes.
10081{_}2088{_}We are holding our ground until we sight the enemy.
10081{_}2089{_}Then we shall retire.
10081{_}2090{_}How long before you will come up with us?"
10081{_}2091{_}"In your present position, two hours.
10081{_}2092{_}If you fall back, we shall, of course, be with you sooner.
10081{_}2093{_}Are you ready for action?"
10081{_}2094{_}"Yes; cleared."
10081{_}2095{_}"Good.
10081{_}2096{_}I am giving my men all the rest possible.
10081{_}2097{_}Goodbye."
10081{_}2098{_}"Funny," said Captain Raleigh to Jack, "they should have sighted the enemy by this time."
10081{_}2099{_}"It would seem so, sir," agreed Jack.
10081{_}2100{_}"Well, they probably will be in sight by the time we come up with the _Glasgow_," said Captain Raleigh.
10081{_}2101{_}But two hours later, when the _Queen Mary_ and _Indefatigable_ came up with the other British ships, no enemy had been sighted yet.
10081{_}2102{_}It was then almost nine o'clock.
10081{_}2103{_}"You are sure you have not miscalculated the time?"
10081{_}2104{_}Captain Raleigh asked of Frank and Jack.
10081{_}2105{_}"Positive, sir," replied the former.
10081{_}2106{_}"Besides, you have the document relating to the attack."
10081{_}2107{_}"True enough.
10081{_}2108{_}The enemy probably has been delayed.
10081{_}2109{_}Or perhaps they will await the coming of daylight."
10081{_}2110{_}"It would be better if they did, for us, I mean, wouldn't it, sir?"
10081{_}2111{_}asked Frank.
10081{_}2112{_}"Much better," replied his commander briefly.
10081{_}2113{_}"Then let us hope that is what happens."
