10081{_}2114{_}"But I am afraid it won't happen," said Jack.
10081{_}2115{_}"If the Germans get this far safely, they won't wait for us to overtake them."
10081{_}2116{_}"No; you're right there," said Captain Raleigh.
10081{_}2117{_}"The thing that worries me is that, if they do get by us, they will spread out all over the sea.
10081{_}2118{_}They will be able to raid the British coast, may succeed in running through the English channel, and then we shall have to round them up all over again.
10081{_}2119{_}They would scatter over the seven seas."
10081{_}2120{_}"Then we've got to lick 'em," declared Frank, grimly.
10081{_}2121{_}Captain Raleigh smiled.
10081{_}2122{_}"That's the spirit I like to see," he said quietly.
10081{_}2123{_}"It is the spirit that has carried the British flag to victory against overwhelming odds on many occasions."
10081{_}2124{_}"But he is not an Englishman, sir," said Jack with a smile.
10081{_}2125{_}"What?"
10081{_}2126{_}exclaimed Captain Raleigh.
10081{_}2127{_}"Not an Englishman?
10081{_}2128{_}Then what is he?"
10081{_}2129{_}"American," was Jack's reply.
10081{_}2130{_}"Oh, well, it amounts practically to the same thing," declared Captain Raleigh.
10081{_}2131{_}"Next to being an American," said Frank, quietly, "I would be English."
10081{_}2132{_}The first officer, Lieutenant MacDonald, burst into the captain's cabin at this moment.
10081{_}2133{_}"Message from the _Glasgow_, sir!"
10081{_}2134{_}he exclaimed.
10081{_}2135{_}"German battle squadron, steaming at twenty knots, sighted five miles off Jutland, sir!"
10081{_}2136{_}CHAPTER XV  THE FIRST GUN   Skagerak, in which the greatest naval battle of history was about to be fought, is an arm of the North Sea between Norway and Denmark.
10081{_}2137{_}The scene of the battle was laid off Jutland and Horn Reef, on the southern extremity of Denmark.
10081{_}2138{_}From the reef of Heligoland, the main German base in the North Sea, to Jutland, is about one hundred miles as the crow flies.
10081{_}2139{_}Therefore, it became evident that the German high sea fleet must have left the protection of that supposedly impregnable fortress some time before.
10081{_}2140{_}That the advance of the German fleet had been well planned was indicated by the very fact that it could successfully elude the British cruisers patrolling the entrance to the mine fields that guarded Heligoland itself.
10081{_}2141{_}Could a British fleet of any size have got between the German high sea fleet and Heligoland the menace of the German fleet would have ended for all time.
10081{_}2142{_}At the moment, however, the British warships were scattered over the North Sea in such a manner as to preclude such an attempt; and the best Admiral Beatty and Admiral Jellicoe could hope for was to come up with the German fleet and give battle, preventing, if possible, the escape of any units of the fleet to other parts of the sea and to drive all that the British could not sink back to Heligoland.
10081{_}2143{_}The German dash of one hundred miles across the North Sea was a bold venture and one that the British had not believed the Germans would attempt at that time.
10081{_}2144{_}British vigilance had been lax or the German fleet could never have gone so far from its base without discovery; and this laxity proved costly for the British; and might even have proven more costly still.
10081{_}2145{_}Above the German fleet came a fleet of aircraft, augmented to a great degree by three powerful Zeppelin balloons.
10081{_}2146{_}Lying low upon the water also was a fleet of German submarines.
10081{_}2147{_}As the German fleet approached Jutland on the night of May 31, it was shrouded in darkness.
10081{_}2148{_}The night was very black and a heavy fog hung over the sea.
10081{_}2149{_}The night could not have been better for the attempt, which would, in all probability have succeeded, had it not been for the fact that the British had been forewarned.
10081{_}2150{_}Forewarned is forearmed; and this fact alone prevented the Germans from carrying out their designs.
10081{_}2151{_}It is history that the approach of the German fleet had been reported to the commander of the British cruiser _Glasgow_ by an aviator, who had sailed across the dark sea in a hydroplane.
10081{_}2152{_}Whether the Germans knew that there were but three British vessels in the Skagerak cannot be told, but certainly they believed they were in sufficient strength to force a passage, particularly by a surprise attack, which they believed the present venture would be.
10081{_}2153{_}Therefore, it must have been a great disappointment to the German admiral when a single big gun boomed in the distance.
10081{_}2154{_}This was the voice of the British battleship _Queen Mary,_ which, taking directions from the _Glasgow's_ aviator, had fired the opening shot, telling the Germans that their approach had been discovered and that the passage of the Skagerak would be contested.
10081{_}2155{_}Immediately the German fleet slowed down; for the German admiral had no means of knowing the strength of the British fleet at that point.
10081{_}2156{_}Hurried orders flashed back and forth.
10081{_}2157{_}A few moments later three aeroplanes, which had been hanging low above the German fleet, dashed forward.
10081{_}2158{_}They had been ordered forth to ascertain the strength of the British.
10081{_}2159{_}In almost less time than it takes to tell it they were directly above the British fleet, which, so far, consisted only of five ships of war-- besides the _Glasgow,_ an armored cruiser, the _Albert_ and _Victoria_, torpedo boats, being the _Queen Mary_ and _Indefatigable_.
10081{_}2160{_}As the Germans approached in the air, a hydroplane ascended from each of the British ships and British aviators gave chase to the enemy.
10081{_}2161{_}One, which had come too close, was brought down; but the other two returned safely to the shelter of the German fleet, where the British dare not follow them because of the presence of a superior force of the enemy.
10081{_}2162{_}But the German aviators had learned what they had been sent to learn.
10081{_}2163{_}They had discovered the strength of the British.
10081{_}2164{_}Again sharp orders were flashed from the German flagship.
10081{_}2165{_}The fleet came on faster.
10081{_}2166{_}Captain Raleigh, because of his seniority, had taken command of the small British squadron.
10081{_}2167{_}He had drawn his ships up in a semicircle, heads pointed to the foe.
10081{_}2168{_}As his aviators signalled that the Germans were again advancing, Captain Raleigh gave the command that had been long eagerly awaited by the men--a command which the commander of the _Queen Mary_ had delayed giving until the last moment because he desired to give his men all the rest he could.
10081{_}2169{_}"Clear for action!"
10081{_}2170{_}he thundered.
10081{_}2171{_}Jack glanced at his watch and as he did so eight bells struck.
10081{_}2172{_}"Midnight!"
10081{_}2173{_}The exclamation was wrung from Frank.
10081{_}2174{_}"And no aid for at least three hours," said Jack, quietly.
10081{_}2175{_}As the lad spoke the fog suddenly lifted and gave to the British a view of the advancing German fleet.
10081{_}2176{_}"Forward turret guns!"
10081{_}2177{_}cried Captain Raleigh, "Fire at will!"
10081{_}2178{_}A terrible salvo burst from the 16-inch guns in the forward turret.
10081{_}2179{_}At almost the same moment the leading German ships opened fire.
10081{_}2180{_}The first few salvos from each side did no damage, for the range had not been gauged accurately.
10081{_}2181{_}It became apparent now that the German admiral had no intention of risking all his first line ships in this encounter.
10081{_}2182{_}Apparently he had decided that his smaller vessels were fully capable of coping with the small number of the enemy that was contesting his advance.
10081{_}2183{_}From the shelter of the larger ships advanced the battle cruisers.
10081{_}2184{_}Not a battleship nor a dreadnaught came forward.
10081{_}2185{_}But the smaller ships dashed on swiftly and presently their guns found the range.
10081{_}2186{_}A shell burst aboard the _Glasgow's_ bridge, carrying away nearly the entire superstructure.
10081{_}2187{_}The captain and his first officer were killed, and many men were injured as huge splinters flew in all directions.
10081{_}2188{_}Under the command of the second officer, the _Glasgow_ fought back.
10081{_}2189{_}A shell from her forward turret burst aboard the closest German vessel and there was a terrific explosion, followed by a series of blasts not so loud.
10081{_}2190{_}Came fearful cries from aboard the enemy.
10081{_}2191{_}And then the whole sky was lighted up for miles around as the German ship sprang into a brilliant sheet of flame.
10081{_}2192{_}For perhaps two minutes it lighted up the heavens; then there was another violent explosion and the German cruiser disappeared beneath the water with a hiss like that of a thousand serpents.
10081{_}2193{_}A cheer rose on the air--a loud British cheer.
10081{_}2194{_}"One gone," said Frank, quietly.
10081{_}2195{_}"Yes, but only one gone," replied Jack.
10081{_}2196{_}"Yes, but it's two o'clock now," said Frank, hopefully.
10081{_}2197{_}"About time to begin our retreat then," said Jack.
10081{_}2198{_}And the order for retreat came a few moments later.
10081{_}2199{_}The five British ships--for all were still able to navigate in spite of the damage that had been inflicted--came about in a broad circle and headed westward.
10081{_}2200{_}Then it was the Germans' time to cheer and they did so with a will.
10081{_}2201{_}It was not often that a British battleship had fled before a German ship or ships and the Germans, since the war opened, had little chance to cheer such a procedure.
10081{_}2202{_}But now that they had such a chance, they cheered their best Apparently, they had lost sight of the fact that the British were retiring before superior numbers, and that, even in spite of that and the fact that they now were retreating, they still had the best of the encounter so far.
10081{_}2203{_}For one German cruiser lay at the bottom of the sea.
10081{_}2204{_}The British retreat was slow; and, for some unaccountable reason, the Germans did not press forward as swiftly as they might have done.
10081{_}2205{_}Whether they feared a trap, or whether the German admiral had determined to await the coming of day before disposing of the enemy, was not apparent.
10081{_}2206{_}But that he had some plan in mind, every Briton realized.
10081{_}2207{_}"The longer he holds off the better," said Frank.
10081{_}2208{_}"Right," agreed Jack.
10081{_}2209{_}"Of course, we probably could run away from them if they pressed us too hard, but we wouldn't; and for that reason he should be able to dispose of us if he came ahead swiftly."
10081{_}2210{_}"Wonder why some of these Zeppelins and airships haven't come into action?"
10081{_}2211{_}said Frank.
10081{_}2212{_}"I don't know.
10081{_}2213{_}Perhaps the Germans are afraid of losing one of them.
10081{_}2214{_}They probably have other uses for them, for, should they break through here, it is likely they have their plans laid.
10081{_}2215{_}What time have you?"
10081{_}2216{_}"Three thirty," said Frank, after a glance at his watch.
10081{_}2217{_}"An hour, almost, till daylight.
10081{_}2218{_}Do you suppose the others will arrive on time?"
10081{_}2219{_}"I hope so.
10081{_}2220{_}It would be better, of course, if they arrived while it is yet dark, for then they might come up unseen.
10081{_}2221{_}But with their arrival we still will be outnumbered; and, realizing that, the Germans, when the day breaks, will press the attack harder."
10081{_}2222{_}"I guess we will manage to hold them till the main fleet arrives in the morning," said Frank, hopefully.
10081{_}2223{_}"We will have to hold them," declared Jack.
10081{_}2224{_}At this moment the lads' attention was directed to the cruiser _Glasgow_.
10081{_}2225{_}Already badly damaged, a second German shell had now burst amidships with a loud explosion.
10081{_}2226{_}"And that settles the _Glasgow_," said Jack, sadly.
10081{_}2227{_}He was right.
10081{_}2228{_}Gamely the _Glasgow_ fought back, but it was apparent to all, in spite of the darkness, that she was settling lower and lower in the water.
10081{_}2229{_}"And we can't rescue the men," said Frank.
10081{_}2230{_}"Remember the admiralty orders.
10081{_}2231{_}No ship in action is to go to the aid of another.
10081{_}2232{_}It would be suicide."
10081{_}2233{_}"So it would," said Jack.
10081{_}2234{_}"Poor fellows."
10081{_}2235{_}Slowly the _Glasgow_ settled; and for a moment the fire of all the other vessels--Germans as well as British--lulled a bit.
10081{_}2236{_}All eyes were bent on the sinking ship.
10081{_}2237{_}A wireless message was flashed from the _Glasgow_ to Captain Raleigh of the _Queen Mary_.
10081{_}2238{_}"Goodbye," it said.
10081{_}2239{_}"Hold them!"
10081{_}2240{_}After that there was no further word from the doomed cruiser.
10081{_}2241{_}The searchlights of both fleets played full upon the _Glasgow_ as she settled lower in the water.
10081{_}2242{_}She staggered, seemed to make an effort to hold herself afloat, and then sank suddenly.
10081{_}2243{_}The duel of big guns broke out afresh.
10081{_}2244{_}CHAPTER XVI  THE BATTLE   Dawn.
10081{_}2245{_}With the breaking of the intense darkness what a surprise was in store for the Germans!
10081{_}2246{_}Back of the four remaining British ships that had at first engaged the Germans, interrupting their dash and holding them in check until the arrival of a force strong enough to engage the foe more closely, came now the relief promised by Vice-Admiral Beatty.
10081{_}2247{_}Gathered from various parts of the North Sea, they had steamed toward Jutland, and, arriving there at almost the same time, they had assumed battle formation in the darkness.
10081{_}2248{_}That the British were approaching must have been known by the German admiral, for their wireless apparatus had been working unceasingly, telling of their approach, and these signals must have been caught by the German warships, though, because sent in code, they were undecipherable.
10081{_}2249{_}Nor could the enemy tell, by the sound, just how close the British were.
10081{_}2250{_}Captain Raleigh, too, as well as the other British commanders, had known the other English ships were forming some distance back.
10081{_}2251{_}Toward these they now retreated; and just as dawn broke, and the British sailors obtained their first view of the promised assistance--and greeted the new arrivals with cheers--the British advanced to the attack.
10081{_}2252{_}The German admiral, taking in the situation, knew that he still outnumbered the British--that the advantage was still with him.
10081{_}2253{_}He determined to give battle.
10081{_}2254{_}He knew, too, that it was only a question of time until the main British fleet would approach and he determined to win the battle before the arrival of new foes.
10081{_}2255{_}He signalled an advance.
10081{_}2256{_}The British fleet was great and powerful--but not so great and powerful as the German by far.
10081{_}2257{_}As the _Queen Mary, Indefatigable_ and the two torpedo boats fell back, still the center of German fire and still hurling shell, seeking their proper places in the battle line, the other British vessels came on.
10081{_}2258{_}And presently the _Queen Mary_ and others had gained their places in the formation.
10081{_}2259{_}Ahead of the larger ships now--the _Queen Mary_, the _Indefatigable_ and the _Invincible,_ advanced the speediest of light cruisers--the _Defense_, the _Biack Prince_ and the _Warrior_.
10081{_}2260{_}Behind these, spread out fan-wise, came the destroyers _Tipperary, Turbulent, Nestore, Alcaster, Fortune, Sparrow Hawk, Ardent_ and the _Shark_.
10081{_}2261{_}The _Albert_ and _Victoria_ also had fallen in line, though badly battered by the effects of the German shells during the night.
10081{_}2262{_}Then the three battle cruisers advanced; and as the battle opened, far back came the battleship _Marlborough_, hurrying to join in the struggle.
10081{_}2263{_}The German fleet advanced to the attack in a broad semi-circle.
10081{_}2264{_}The flagship, the _Westphalen_, a dreadnaught of 18,600 tons, was squarely in the center.
10081{_}2265{_}To her left was the battleship _Pommern_ and next the _Freiderich_; to her right the battleships _Wiesbaden_ and _Frauenlob_.
10081{_}2266{_}Beyond the battleships to the left were the cruisers _Hindenburg_ and _Lutzow_, and beyond the battleships to the right the cruisers _Elbing_ and _Essen_.
10081{_}2267{_}Torpedo boats, more than a score of them, also spread far on either side.
10081{_}2268{_}Directly behind the single dreadnaught and the battleships came a flotilla of submarines, ready to dash forward at the proper moment and launch their deadly torpedoes.
10081{_}2269{_}Overhead, and moving forward, were the three giant Zeppelins and a flotilla of other aircraft.
10081{_}2270{_}Of all the vessels engaged, the _Queen Mary_ was the largest.
10081{_}2271{_}The _Marlborough_, advancing rapidly, came next and then the German dreadnaught _Westphalen_.
10081{_}2272{_}The British battle cruisers _Indefatigable_ and _Invincible_ were the next most powerful, in the order named, and the other German vessels were by far superior to the British.
10081{_}2273{_}Now, as the battle opened with the greatest fury, another British vessel was sighted to the westward.
10081{_}2274{_}It was the _Lion_, the flagship of Vice-Admiral Beatty, steaming at full speed ahead.
10081{_}2275{_}Over the tops of the three British cruisers, light vessels travelled swiftly toward the enemy, the larger ships opened with their big guns.
10081{_}2276{_}The range was found almost with the first salvo and shells began to drop aboard the enemy.
10081{_}2277{_}The British cruiser _Defense_, making straight for the German dreadnaught _Westphalen_, hurled a shell aboard the German flagship that burst amidships.
10081{_}2278{_}There was a terrible explosion and men were hurled into the water in little pieces.
10081{_}2279{_}A hole was blown through the upper deck.
10081{_}2280{_}But the _Defense_ paid dearly for this act.
10081{_}2281{_}The forward guns of the _Westphalen_ poured a veritable rain of shells upon the British vessel and in a moment she was wounded unto death.
10081{_}2282{_}There was nothing the other vessels of the fleet could do to aid her; and it was plainly apparent that she must sink.
10081{_}2283{_}But the British tars stuck to their guns and they continued to hurl shells into the German line until the water of the North Sea washed over them.
10081{_}2284{_}The _Defense_ was gone.
10081{_}2285{_}This left the _Black Prince_ and the _Warrior_ alone before the larger British vessels and they stood to their work gallantly.
10081{_}2286{_}The fire of both cruisers was centered on the German flagship; and it was plain that if they continued at their work the _Westphalen_ was doomed.
10081{_}2287{_}An order was flashed to the German Zeppelins.
10081{_}2288{_}Two sped forward.
10081{_}2289{_}Captain Raleigh of the _Queen Mary_ saw them advancing and the forward anti-aircraft gun was unloosened.
10081{_}2290{_}The first Zeppelin, flying low, was pierced before it had moved forward a hundred yards; and it fell into the sea between the German battleships, a flaming mass.
10081{_}2291{_}But the second came on.
10081{_}2292{_}Above the _Black Prince_ the Zeppelin paused.
10081{_}2293{_}Something dropped through the air.
10081{_}2294{_}There was a flash, an explosion and a dense black cloud rolled across the water.
10081{_}2295{_}When it had cleared the _Black Prince_ was gone!
10081{_}2296{_}The anti-aircraft guns of the _Queen Mary_ and the _Indefatigable_ fired furiously at the Zeppelin; and a few moments later a shot from the latter struck home.
10081{_}2297{_}The second Zeppelin fell into the sea.
10081{_}2298{_}By this time the _Marlborough_ had drawn up with the _Queen Mary_ and the other large British ships; and now these advanced majestically.
10081{_}2299{_}The first to encounter the weight of their guns was the German battleship _Pommern_, of 12,900 tons.
10081{_}2300{_}Raked fore and aft, she was soon ablaze.
10081{_}2301{_}Her crew leaped into the sea, almost as one man, following an explosion in her boiler room; and the water was dark with bobbing heads.
10081{_}2302{_}The _Pommern's_ sister ship, the _Freiderich_, slowed down and gave assistance in picking up the crew of the former vessel; and while she was engaged in this work no British gun fired at her.
10081{_}2303{_}Gradually the _Marlborough_, the _Queen Mary_, the _Indefatigable_ and the _Invincible_ drew closer together as they advanced upon the Germans.
10081{_}2304{_}Shells burst over them with regularity, but so far none had reached a vital spot.
10081{_}2305{_}The _Queen Mary_ turned all her forward guns on the _Westphalen_ and raked her fore and aft.
10081{_}2306{_}In vain the other vessels of the German fleet sought to detract the _Queen Mary's_ fire.
10081{_}2307{_}Captain Raleigh had started out with the intention of disposing of the German flagship and he was determined not to heed the others until the _Westphalen_ had been sent to the bottom.
10081{_}2308{_}It was no easy task he had set for himself, for he now was the center of fire of the whole German fleet--almost.
10081{_}2309{_}A submarine darted forward to save the _Westphalen_.
10081{_}2310{_}The quick eye of a British gunner caught it.
10081{_}2311{_}He took aim and fired.
10081{_}2312{_}The submarine disappeared.
10081{_}2313{_}With a view to disposing of the enemy immediately, Captain Raleigh ordered that one of the two forward torpedoes be launched.
10081{_}2314{_}There was a hiss as the little tube was released.
10081{_}2315{_}The distance was so close now that a miss was impossible.
10081{_}2316{_}There was an instant of silence, followed by a terrible rending sound; then a loud blast.
10081{_}2317{_}The torpedo had reached the _Westphalen's_ boiler room.
10081{_}2318{_}Quickly the German admiral and his officers clambered over the side and rowed to the _Wiesbaden_, where they were taken on board and the admiral's flag run up.
10081{_}2319{_}The _Westphalen_ was abandoned; and she sank a few moments later.
10081{_}2320{_}In the meantime, the British cruiser _Warrior_, of 13,500 tons, had been sent down by the explosion of a German shell which had reached her magazine.
10081{_}2321{_}So rapidly had she settled that not a man of her crew escaped.
10081{_}2322{_}Thus had the three light battle cruisers of the British--the vessels that had shown the way--been disposed of.
10081{_}2323{_}At this moment Vice-Admiral Beatty and his flagship, the _Lion_, entered the battle.
10081{_}2324{_}The great guns of the flagship roared above the others and the battleship _Frauenlob_, singled out by her fire, soon sank.
10081{_}2325{_}In spite of the German losses, the British, so far, had had the worst of the encounter and the German admiral, despite the loss of his flagship, had no mind to give up the battle.
10081{_}2326{_}He pushed to closer quarters.
10081{_}2327{_}Now the fighting became more terrific.
10081{_}2328{_}Shells struck upon all ships engaged at intervals of a few seconds apart.
10081{_}2329{_}Frequently loud explosions were heard above the voices of the great guns; and in most cases these signified the end of a ship of war.
10081{_}2330{_}Among the smaller vessels--the torpedo boats--which had singled each other out, the execution had been terrible.
10081{_}2331{_}Dead and wounded strewed the decks and there was no time for the uninjured to give aid.
10081{_}2332{_}They were too busy attending to their guns and manoeuvering their vessels.
10081{_}2333{_}But the outcome of an engagement such as this could have but one result, it seemed.
10081{_}2334{_}Outnumbered as they were and fighting as bravely as they knew how, the British were getting the worst of it.
10081{_}2335{_}Rather than sacrifice more lives and ships, Vice-Admiral Beatty, on the _Lion_, gave the signal to retire.
10081{_}2336{_}He was in hopes that the Germans would follow and thus fall into the clutches of the main British fleet which was advancing at full speed and with which Vice-Admiral Beatty had been in communication by wireless.
10081{_}2337{_}The Germans accepted the bait as the British drew off slowly; and as they advanced more ships steamed up from the east.
10081{_}2338{_}It was a second German squadron advancing to the aid of the first.
10081{_}2339{_}There was a cry of surprise from the British, for they had not known that there was a second fleet in such close proximity.
10081{_}2340{_}These new vessels evidently were the reserves the German admiral had been depending upon to turn the tide of battle should his first line ships not be able to overcome the British.
10081{_}2341{_}Seeing apparent victory within his grasp, the German admiral signalled his fleet to full speed; so the British retreated more rapidly.
10081{_}2342{_}Suddenly there was a terrible explosion to the right of the _Queen Mary_.
10081{_}2343{_}Frank and Jack, as well as all others on the _Queen Mary_, gazed in that direction.
10081{_}2344{_}The battle cruiser _Invincible_ suddenly sprang into a sheet of flame and parted in half.
10081{_}2345{_}A German shell had struck her vitals.
10081{_}2346{_}A cry of despair broke from the British as the _Invincible_--the greatest British ship to suffer so far--dived beneath the waves.
10081{_}2347{_}CHAPTER XVII  THE MAIN FLEET ARRIVES   It was by a miracle, it seemed, that the _Queen Mary,_ the _Indefatigable_, the _Marlborough_ and the _Lion_, now in the front line, had escaped being struck in their vitals by the German shells that flew all about.
10081{_}2348{_}On the _Queen Mary_, dead men and wounded men strewed the deck.
10081{_}2349{_}They were being carried below as rapidly as possible, where the ship's surgeon, with a corps of assistants, was attending to their wounds.
10081{_}2350{_}Frank and Jack had been working like demons.
10081{_}2351{_}From one part of the ship to the other they had been running with orders ever since the battle opened.
10081{_}2352{_}The heart of each lad was in his throat--not because of fear-- but because the British were getting the worst of the engagement.
10081{_}2353{_}Never before had they seen an enemy fleet stand up to a British squadron of this size and fight.
10081{_}2354{_}Always before it had been the German policy to run.
10081{_}2355{_}But now they were not only standing up to the British, but were giving them a bad thrashing.
10081{_}2356{_}Each lad realized, of course, that the British were out-numbered and that the weight of guns was in favor of the enemy; but in spite of this they felt that the enemy should be defeated.
10081{_}2357{_}They cast occasional glances to the west, hoping to catch sight of the main British fleet, which should be drawing near now.
10081{_}2358{_}But at nine o'clock there was no smoke on the horizon.
10081{_}2359{_}The loss of the _Invincible_ had been a hard blow to the British.
10081{_}2360{_}As the others retreated now the Germans pressed them closely.
10081{_}2361{_}A shot struck the _Marlborough_ in the forward turret, exploding her guns there and killing the gun crews.
10081{_}2362{_}The effect of the explosion was terrible.
10081{_}2363{_}Men were hurled high in the air and came down in small pieces.
10081{_}2364{_}Jack, in the forward turret of the _Queen Mary_ a moment later, was hurled to the deck as a German shell struck one of the guns and blew it to pieces.
10081{_}2365{_}The lad escaped the rain of steel that descended a moment later, but others in the turret were not so fortunate.
10081{_}2366{_}Fully half the men there were killed or wounded so badly that they could fight no more.
10081{_}2367{_}Jack sprang to one of the guns himself.
10081{_}2368{_}It was loaded.
10081{_}2369{_}Quickly the lad sighted it upon one of the enemy ships and fired.
10081{_}2370{_}He watched the effect of this shot.
10081{_}2371{_}It was the German cruiser _Elbing_ at which he had aimed.
10081{_}2372{_}He saw a cloud of missiles ascend from amidships and knew that the shot had struck home.
10081{_}2373{_}Jack forgot all about reporting to Captain Raleigh for further orders, and as the battle raged, he continued to fire one of the big 16-inch guns--he and other unwounded British tars.
10081{_}2374{_}Frank had not seen his chum for an hour; and chancing to poke his head into the forward turret, he was surprised to see Jack working like a Trojan with the members of the gun crew.
10081{_}2375{_}"Good work, Jack!
10081{_}2376{_}Keep it up!"
10081{_}2377{_}he called.
10081{_}2378{_}Jack looked in Frank's direction long enough to wave his hand; then turned back to his work.
10081{_}2379{_}Came a loud British cheer.
10081{_}2380{_}"What's happened?"
10081{_}2381{_}demanded Jack of the man next him, shouting at the top of his voice to make himself heard above the din of battle.
10081{_}2382{_}The man shook his head.
10081{_}2383{_}"Don't know," he shouted back, "unless the main fleet has been sighted."
10081{_}2384{_}"We might have sunk one of the enemy," said another.
10081{_}2385{_}As a matter of fact, both men were right.
10081{_}2386{_}Two German torpedo boats had gone to the bottom almost simultaneously under well directed British shots; and, far back across the sea, a flotilla of battleships had been sighted.
10081{_}2387{_}Apparently the Germans had not yet sighted the British reinforcements, for they continued to press their foes hard.
10081{_}2388{_}Four British torpedo boats had been sent to the bottom of the sea.
10081{_}2389{_}They were the _Tipperary_, the _Turbulent_, the _Nestore_ and the _Shark_.
10081{_}2390{_}The others gave slowly before the enemy; and a moment later two of those sank--the _Sparrow Hawk_ and the _Ardent_.
10081{_}2391{_}There now remained facing the entire German fleet the _Lion_, the _Queen Mary_, the _Indefatigable_, the _Marlborough_ and two torpedo boats, the _Fortune_ and the _Alcaster_.
10081{_}2392{_}But the German losses had been great.
10081{_}2393{_}The _Westphalen_ had been sunk.
10081{_}2394{_}So had the _Pommern_ and the _Freiderich_.
10081{_}2395{_}The _Frauenlob_ had gone to the bottom and the _Wiesbaden_, the new flagship, was badly crippled.
10081{_}2396{_}As another German torpedo boat sank, the Germans slackened their pace.
10081{_}2397{_}The British had a breathing spell.
10081{_}2398{_}But the battle was not over yet.
10081{_}2399{_}The second German squadron had now approached almost close enough to take a hand in the battle.
10081{_}2400{_}Apparently this Was what the German admiral was waiting for before resuming operations.
10081{_}2401{_}It was plainly evident now that the Germans had sighted the approaching British fleet, but at that distance they were unable to make out its strength.
10081{_}2402{_}The German admiral decided to continue the battle if he could do so with any hope of success.
10081{_}2403{_}So, with the second squadron in range, he gave the command to advance again.
10081{_}2404{_}The _Queen Mary_ and the _Indefatigable_ bore the brunt of this next attack and for half an hour it seemed that it was impossible for the two ships to live through the rain of shells that fell all about them.
10081{_}2405{_}But live they did and they gave as good or better than they received.
10081{_}2406{_}The German battleship _Hindenburg_, pierced by half a dozen shells at almost the same time, staggered back and fell out of line.
10081{_}2407{_}But the British had no mercy on her.
10081{_}2408{_}Shell after shell they poured upon her; and at last she sank.
10081{_}2409{_}The _Wiesbaden_, the German flagship, pressed hotly to the attack.
10081{_}2410{_}Although struck in a dozen places and her port side batteries out of commission, she continued to play on the _Queen Mary_ and the _Indefatigable_ with her forward turret guns.
10081{_}2411{_}As a matter of fact, it was fortunate for the _Queen Mary_ and the _Indefatigable_ that they had begun to retire; for their forward turret guns had been silenced and the only pieces that they could now bring into play were in the turrets aft.
10081{_}2412{_}A shell from the German battleship _Lutzow_ exploded on the bridge of the _Marlborough_.
10081{_}2413{_}The bridge was carried completely away and the commander of the ship was killed, as were half a score of other officers.
10081{_}2414{_}A second shell struck the _Marlborough_ and carried away her steering apparatus.
10081{_}2415{_}Absolutely uncontrollable now, the _Marlborough_ drifted toward the _Lion_, with which she almost collided before the _Lion_ could get out of the way.
10081{_}2416{_}There was nothing that could be done for her until after the battle, at any rate, and the others left her to her fate.
10081{_}2417{_}Drifting as she was, the _Marlborough_ continued her fire; and of a sudden she put a shot aboard the _Lutzow_ in a vital spot.
10081{_}2418{_}The _Lutzow_ blew up with a terrible roar.
10081{_}2419{_}The crew of the _Marlborough_ cheered and waved their hands to their companions on the other British ships.
10081{_}2420{_}Apparently this was more than the German admiral had bargained for.
10081{_}2421{_}With his whole second squadron intact and the British apparently helpless, he had thought to crush these few ships before aid should reach them; and then, if the approaching British were not too formidable, to offer them battle also.
10081{_}2422{_}Now there were only three British ships in line--the _Lion_, the _Queen Mary_ and the _Indefatigable_--and these were really not fit nor able to continue the fight.
10081{_}2423{_}But the men fought on doggedly.
10081{_}2424{_}None of the others had thought of surrender and no such idea entered the head of a single man aboard any of the British ships.
10081{_}2425{_}Help was at hand and then the Germans would get the thrashing of their lives, the men told themselves.
10081{_}2426{_}They would keep the Germans busy until this help arrived.
10081{_}2427{_}Hardly a man aboard the _Queen Mary_ that had not been wounded.
10081{_}2428{_}Sweat poured from their faces, hands and body as they continued to fight their guns; and as they fought they shouted and yelled encouragement to one another.
10081{_}2429{_}"Boom!"
10081{_}2430{_}There was a different tone to this deep voice and every man on board the hard pressed British ships knew what it meant.
10081{_}2431{_}The first ship of the main British fleet had come within range and had opened with her biggest gun.
10081{_}2432{_}Other new voices took up the challenge and within a few moments the roar of battle was at its height once more.
10081{_}2433{_}Still a considerable distance away, the dimensions of the approaching British fleet now became apparent to the German admiral.
10081{_}2434{_}He had thought, at first, that perhaps the newcomers would number a few ships, attracted by the sounds of battle, but as he looked at the formidable array now bearing down on him he knew that his plans, whatever they were, had been frustrated.
10081{_}2435{_}"And we had it all planned so carefully," he said between clenched teeth.
10081{_}2436{_}He strode up and down angrily, beating the palm of one hand with a knotted fist.
10081{_}2437{_}"How could they have learned of it?"
10081{_}2438{_}he cried.
10081{_}2439{_}"How could they?"
10081{_}2440{_}He was very angry.
10081{_}2441{_}An officer approached him.
10081{_}2442{_}"Shall we draw off, sir?"
10081{_}2443{_}he asked, and pointed to the fresh British ships bearing down on them.
10081{_}2444{_}"No!"
10081{_}2445{_}thundered the admiral.
10081{_}2446{_}"Why don't you sink those three ships ahead of you there?
10081{_}2447{_}Sink them, I tell you!"
10081{_}2448{_}The officer saluted and moved away.
10081{_}2449{_}For some moments the German admiral continued to talk to himself in great anger; then he suddenly cooled down.
10081{_}2450{_}With a finger he summoned the officer who had accosted him a moment before.
10081{_}2451{_}The officer approached and saluted.
10081{_}2452{_}"I forgot myself a moment ago," said the admiral.
10081{_}2453{_}"You may give the signal to retire!"
10081{_}2454{_}A moment later the big German ships began to come about; and from the decks of the _Queen Mary_, the _Lion_ and the _Indefatigable_ there came loud British cheers.
10081{_}2455{_}The _Marlborough_, still helpless, poured shell after shell upon the enemy.
10081{_}2456{_}Some distance away still, the British fleet was approaching in an endeavor to intercept the retreat of the enemy.
10081{_}2457{_}Captain Raleigh of the _Queen Mary_ took in the situation at a glance.
10081{_}2458{_}"They'll never do it!"
10081{_}2459{_}he exclaimed.
10081{_}2460{_}He determined upon a bold step.
10081{_}2461{_}He gave command to bring the _Queen Mary_ about.
10081{_}2462{_}Then, disabled as his ship was, he started in pursuit of the enemy.
10081{_}2463{_}There was a cheer from the _Indefatigable_, and presently the head of that vessel also came about She started after the _Queen Mary_!
10081{_}2464{_}CHAPTER XVIII  THE SINKING OF THE "QUEEN MARY"   Perceiving this move by two vessels that he believed the same as at the bottom of, the sea, so far as fighting purposes went, the German admiral became very angry again.
10081{_}2465{_}"A blight on these English!"
10081{_}2466{_}he exclaimed.
10081{_}2467{_}"Don't they know when they are beaten?"
10081{_}2468{_}Certainly it seemed not, if the Admiral's version that they were defeated was correct.
10081{_}2469{_}The _Queen Mary_ and the _Indefatigable_ steamed after the enemy at full speed.
10081{_}2470{_}Jack had relinquished his duties in the gun turret to more experienced hands and had joined Frank on deck.
10081{_}2471{_}To some extent the forward turret had been repaired and was now in condition to hurl more shells after the fleeing enemy.
10081{_}2472{_}It was well after noon when the Germans fled; and as the two British ships followed close on the heels of the enemy--with the main British fleet still some distance back--one of those deep impenetrable fogs that often impede progress on the North Sea suddenly descended.
10081{_}2473{_}It was indeed a boon to the fleeing Germans, for without its aid, there is little likelihood that they could have escaped the British fleet, which had the heels of the enemy.
10081{_}2474{_}But the fog blotted the foe completely from the sight of the main British fleet; and even from the decks of the _Queen Mary_ and the _Indefatigable_, much closer, it was impossible to make out the whereabouts of the Germans.
10081{_}2475{_}The British continued to fire ahead into the fog, but with what result it was impossible to tell.
10081{_}2476{_}The fog became more dense until it was impossible to see ten yards ahead.
10081{_}2477{_}Even the great searchlights on the vessels failed to penetrate the gloom.
10081{_}2478{_}"Well, I guess that settles it," said Frank.
10081{_}2479{_}"Looks that way," Jack agreed.
10081{_}2480{_}"These Germans are pretty slippery customers anyhow.
10081{_}2481{_}It's impossible to catch them in the dark."
10081{_}2482{_}"This fog descended as though it were all made to order for them," Frank complained.
10081{_}2483{_}"Pretty hard to beat a fellow when the elements are fighting on his side," Jack admitted.
10081{_}2484{_}"I imagine Captain Raleigh will give up the chase now."
10081{_}2485{_}But Jack was wrong, though, as it turned out, it would have been a great deal better for all concerned if the chase had been abandoned at that point.
10081{_}2486{_}After some conversation with Captain Reynolds of the _Indefatigable_ by wireless, Captain Raleigh announced that the pursuit would be continued and ordered full speed ahead in the deep darkness.
10081{_}2487{_}As the vessel gathered momentum, Frank exclaimed:  "I don't like this.
10081{_}2488{_}I feel as though something disastrous was about to happen."
10081{_}2489{_}"Another one of those things, eh?"
10081{_}2490{_}said Jack, grinning in the darkness that enveloped them.
10081{_}2491{_}"What things?"
10081{_}2492{_}"I never can remember what you call them.
10081{_}2493{_}Premonitions, I mean."
10081{_}2494{_}"You mean a hunch," said Frank, quietly.
10081{_}2495{_}"Yes, that's just what I have --a hunch."
10081{_}2496{_}"Take it to Captain Raleigh.
10081{_}2497{_}Maybe he will give you something for it," said his friend.
10081{_}2498{_}"This is no joking matter," declared Frank.
10081{_}2499{_}"I'm not naturally nervous, as you know, but right now my nerves are on edge."
10081{_}2500{_}"Just the after effects of the battle," said Jack, quietly.
10081{_}2501{_}"You are all unstrung."
10081{_}2502{_}"I'm unstrung, all right," Frank admitted, "but the battle had nothing to do with it.
10081{_}2503{_}I tell you something is going to happen."
10081{_}2504{_}"Well, what?"
10081{_}2505{_}"I don't know."
10081{_}2506{_}"It's a poor hunch, unless it will tell you what is going to happen," declared Jack.
10081{_}2507{_}"Have it your own way," said Frank.
10081{_}2508{_}"But wait."
10081{_}2509{_}"I'm waiting," said Jack, cheerfully.
10081{_}2510{_}The _Indefatigable_ also, following Captain Reynold's wireless conversation with Captain Raleigh, had dashed after the retreating Germans at full speed.
10081{_}2511{_}Gradually, although in the darkness neither their commanders nor anyone else on board realized it, the _Queen Mary_ and the _Indefatigable_, dashing ahead at full speed as they were, were drawing closer together at every turn of the screws.
10081{_}2512{_}Frank's forebodings were about to bear fruit.
10081{_}2513{_}Now, in the darkness, the vessels were running upon about even terms, but the bows were both pointed toward an angle that would drive them together in collision about a mile distant.
10081{_}2514{_}Although none realized it, this is what would happen unless the fog lifted suddenly.
10081{_}2515{_}But the fog did not lift.
10081{_}2516{_}Frank, try as he would could not shake off his spell.
10081{_}2517{_}"I tell you."
10081{_}2518{_}he said again to his chum, "something is going to happen --and it's going to happen soon."
10081{_}2519{_}There was so much force behind Frank's words--the lad seemed in such deadly earnest--that Jack grew alarmed.
10081{_}2520{_}He had had some experience with these premonitions of Frank's.
10081{_}2521{_}"What is it?"
10081{_}2522{_}he asked anxiously.
10081{_}2523{_}"I wish I knew," said Frank.
10081{_}2524{_}"I----"  Came a sudden shout forward; a cry from the bridge.
10081{_}2525{_}Instinctively, Frank threw out a hand and grasped Jack by the arm.
10081{_}2526{_}Another series of startled cries, the tinkling of a bell in the engine room; a shock as the engines were reversed--but it was too late.
10081{_}2527{_}The two British warships came together with a terrible crash!
10081{_}2528{_}So great was the force of the shock that Frank, standing on the far side, was thrown clear over the rail.
10081{_}2529{_}But the lad's grasp upon his chum's arm was so tight that it dragged Jack along with him; and the two boys fell into the sea together.
10081{_}2530{_}Aboard both British ships all was confusion now.
10081{_}2531{_}With startled cries, men rushed on deck.
10081{_}2532{_}Unable to see in the dense fog, they became panic stricken.
10081{_}2533{_}While these same men would have faced death bravely in battle, they were completely bewildered at this moment.
10081{_}2534{_}In vain the officers aboard both vessels sought to bring some semblance of order out of the confusion.
10081{_}2535{_}Something had gone wrong with the electric lighting apparatus on both vessels.
10081{_}2536{_}There was no light.
10081{_}2537{_}The fog was as thick as ever.
10081{_}2538{_}The crews stampeded for the rails, but at the rails they hesitated, for they did not wish to throw themselves into the great unknown.
10081{_}2539{_}Next came the stampede for life preservers.
10081{_}2540{_}Men fought over their possession, whereas, in cooler moments, hardly a man aboard either ship who would not willingly have given the life preservers to companions.
10081{_}2541{_}Had the men thrown themselves into the sea immediately, it is likely that many of them would have been saved; but their hesitation cost them dearly.
10081{_}2542{_}In vain did the reversed engines of both ships work.
10081{_}2543{_}The sharp steel bow of the _Indefatigable_ had become so firmly embedded in the side of the _Queen Mary_ that it could not be unloosened.
10081{_}2544{_}And so the two battleships sank, together in their last moments as they had been when they had faced almost certain destruction under the muzzles of the great German guns such a short time before.
10081{_}2545{_}Now men from both ships hurled themselves into the sea in an effort to cheat the waters of their prey.
10081{_}2546{_}Commanders and officers, however, realizing that there was no hope of life even in the sea, so swiftly were the ships sinking, stood calmly on the bridges and awaited the end.
10081{_}2547{_}For, they realized, the suction would be so strong when the vessels took their final plunge, that all those anywhere near in the water would be drawn under.
10081{_}2548{_}Captain Raleigh sent a hail across the water in a loud voice.
10081{_}2549{_}"Are you there, Reynolds?"
10081{_}2550{_}"Right here, Raleigh," came back the response.
10081{_}2551{_}"There is no hope here.
10081{_}2552{_}How about you?"
10081{_}2553{_}"No hope here either," was Captain Raleigh's answer.
10081{_}2554{_}"Goodbye, then," shouted Captain Reynolds.
10081{_}2555{_}"Goodbye, old man!"
10081{_}2556{_}They were the last words spoken by these two old friends, who had been boys together, schoolmates and bosom companions.
10081{_}2557{_}Suddenly the two ships took their final plunge.
10081{_}2558{_}Men still on board, those of the crew who had been frightened and had not cast themselves into the sea, straightened instinctively as they felt the vessels give beneath them.
10081{_}2559{_}In the presence of death--when they knew it had arrived-- they were as brave and courageous as in the midst of battle.
10081{_}2560{_}So there was silence aboard the _Queen Mary_ and aboard the _Indefatigable_ as the waves parted for their coming.
10081{_}2561{_}All on board, officers and members of the two crews as well, stood calmly, waiting for the dark waters to close over them.
10081{_}2562{_}The two ships made a last desperate effort to resist the call of the sea.
10081{_}2563{_}They failed.
10081{_}2564{_}A moment later they disappeared from sight.
10081{_}2565{_}No sound came from the depths.
10081{_}2566{_}When Frank and Jack had felt themselves in the water, the latter, realizing immediately what would happen if the ships sank before they had put some distance in between them, struck out swiftly toward what he felt to be the south, giving Frank a hand as he did so.
10081{_}2567{_}The latter recovered himself a moment later, however, and gasped.
10081{_}2568{_}"I'm all right, Jack.
10081{_}2569{_}Let me swim for myself."
10081{_}2570{_}"All right," said Jack, "but keep close beside me.
10081{_}2571{_}We'll have to hurry or we shall be pulled under by the suction when the ships sink."
10081{_}2572{_}Keeping close together they swam with powerful strokes.
10081{_}2573{_}And so it was that they were out of harm's way when the two ships disappeared from sight with a deafening roar as the waters closed over them; they were beyond reach of the suction.
10081{_}2574{_}"There they go," said Frank, sadly.
10081{_}2575{_}"And it is only a miracle that prevented us from going with them," said Jack.
10081{_}2576{_}"We might as well have gone as to be in the middle of the North Sea," said Frank.
10081{_}2577{_}"Nonsense.
10081{_}2578{_}While there's life there's hope."
10081{_}2579{_}They swam on.
10081{_}2580{_}Suddenly Jack's hand came in contact with something in the darkness.
10081{_}2581{_}"A man!"
10081{_}2582{_}he exclaimed.
10081{_}2583{_}"What did you think I was?
10081{_}2584{_}A fish?"
10081{_}2585{_}came the reply.
10081{_}2586{_}"I've a right to escape as well as you."
10081{_}2587{_}"Who are you?"
10081{_}2588{_}asked Frank.
10081{_}2589{_}At that moment, as suddenly as it had descended, the fog lifted.
10081{_}2590{_}Jack looked at the other man in the water and uttered an exclamation of pleasure.
10081{_}2591{_}"Harris!"
10081{_}2592{_}he cried.
10081{_}2593{_}CHAPTER XIX  ADRIFT   The great naval battle of Jutland was over.
10081{_}2594{_}The British fleet now had given up pursuit of the fleeing Germans and Vice-Admiral Beatty paused to take stock of his losses; and they were enormous.
10081{_}2595{_}Three great battle cruisers had gone to the bottom--the _Queen Mary_, of 27,000 tons; the _Indefatigable_, of 18,750 tons, and the _Invincible_, of 17,250 tons.
10081{_}2596{_}Cruisers lost included the _Defense_, of 14,600 tons; the _Black Prince_; of 13,550 tons, and the _Warrior_, of 13,550 tons.
10081{_}2597{_}The giant battle cruiser _Marlborough,_ of 27,500 tons, had been badly damaged, as had the _Lion_ and other vessels.
10081{_}2598{_}The destroyers _Tipperary, Turbulent, Nestore, Alcaster, Fortune, Sparrow Hawk, Ardent_ and _Shark_ had been sunk.
10081{_}2599{_}Total losses ran high into the millions and in the number of men above 7,000.
10081{_}2600{_}The German losses had been less, but nevertheless, taking into consideration damage done to the effectiveness of the two fleets as a whole, the enemy had sustained the harder blow.
10081{_}2601{_}The British fleet still maintained control of the North Sea, while the Germans, because of their losses, had been deprived of a large part of the fighting strength of their fleet.
10081{_}2602{_}The British, in spite of their heavier losses, would recover more quickly than could the enemy.
10081{_}2603{_}The dreadnaught _Westphalen_ was the largest ship lost by the Germans.
10081{_}2604{_}It was of 18,600 tons.
10081{_}2605{_}The three German battleships lost, the _Pommern_, the _Freiderich_ and the _Frauenlob_, were each of 13,350 tons.
10081{_}2606{_}Four battle cruisers had been sent to the bottom.
10081{_}2607{_}They were the _Elbing_, the _Essen_, the _Lutzow_ and the _Hindenburg_, each of 14,400 tons.
10081{_}2608{_}The German losses in torpedo destroyers had been particularly heavy, an even dozen having been sent to the bottom.
10081{_}2609{_}Besides this, the enemy had lost three submarines and two Zeppelin airships, besides a number of smaller aircraft.
10081{_}2610{_}In men the Germans had lost slightly less than the British.
10081{_}2611{_}And so both British and Germans counted the battle a victory; the Germans because in total tonnage sunk they had the best of it; the British, because they held the scene of battle when the fighting was over and because the enemy had retired.
10081{_}2612{_}But, no matter with which side rested the victory, there was no gainsaying the fact that the battle of Jutland was the greatest naval struggle of all time.
10081{_}2613{_}After giving up pursuit of the enemy, the British withdrew.
10081{_}2614{_}Damage to the various vessels was repaired as well as could be done at sea and the ships in need of a more thorough overhauling steamed for England, where they would go into dry-dock.
10081{_}2615{_}The bulk of the British fleet, however, still in perfect fighting trim, again took up the task of patrolling the North Sea, that no German vessels might make their escape from the fortress of Heligoland, for which point the enemy headed immediately after the battle.
10081{_}2616{_}In spite of the severe losses of the Germans, the return of the high sea fleet to Heligoland was marked by a grand ovation by the civil population.
10081{_}2617{_}Various reports were circulated on the island, and all through Germany for that matter.
10081{_}2618{_}One report had it that the entire British fleet had been sent to the bottom; and Berlin, and all Germany, rejoiced.
10081{_}2619{_}But as time passed and the German fleet still remained secure behind its fortifications, the German people began to realize that the victory had not been so great as they had been led to believe.
10081{_}2620{_}They knew they had been fooled; and they vented their anger in many ways.
10081{_}2621{_}Street riots occurred in Berlin and in others of the large cities.
10081{_}2622{_}The people demanded to be told the facts.
10081{_}2623{_}Later they were told, in a measure, but even then they were denied the whole truth.
10081{_}2624{_}So conditions in the central empires grew from bad to worse.
10081{_}2625{_}Jack and Frank, struggling in the water where they had been hurled by the collision of the _Queen Mary_ and the _Indefatigable_, were glad of the company of Harris, who had bobbed up so suddenly alongside of them in the darkness.
10081{_}2626{_}Harris greeted Jack's exclamation of surprise with a grin.
10081{_}2627{_}"Yes; it's me," he replied, discarding his grammar absolutely; "and I'm glad to see you fellows again.
10081{_}2628{_}Question is, what are we going to do now?"
10081{_}2629{_}"Well, you know as much about it as I do," declared Jack.
10081{_}2630{_}"I haven't any idea how far we are from shore, but I am afraid it is farther than we can swim."
10081{_}2631{_}All three cast their eyes over the water.
10081{_}2632{_}There was not a spar nor other piece of wreckage in sight.
10081{_}2633{_}But Jack made out a few moments later, some distance to the east, what appeared to be a ship of some sort.
10081{_}2634{_}He called the attention of the others to it.
10081{_}2635{_}"Suppose we might as well head in that direction, then," declared Harris.
10081{_}2636{_}"Right," agreed Frank.
10081{_}2637{_}He struck out vigorously and the others did the same.
10081{_}2638{_}It was a long ways to that little speck on the water and the lads knew that if the vessel were moving away from them they probably would be lost.
10081{_}2639{_}But at that distance the vessel seemed to be stationary, so they did not give up hope.
10081{_}2640{_}Half an hour later Frank exclaimed: "We're making headway.
10081{_}2641{_}Ship must be standing still."
10081{_}2642{_}"Well, I wish it would come this way," declared Harris.
10081{_}2643{_}"We're still a long way from safety."
10081{_}2644{_}"It's probably a German, anyhow," said Jack, "so if we are rescued it will be only to be made prisoners."
10081{_}2645{_}"That's better than being made shark bait," said Harris; "and, by the way, speaking of sharks, I have heard that there were many of them in these waters."
10081{_}2646{_}Frank shuddered; for he had a wholesome disgust for the man eaters.
10081{_}2647{_}"Hope they don't smell us," he said.
10081{_}2648{_}"And so do I," agreed Jack.
10081{_}2649{_}"We couldn't hope to fight them off, for we have no arms."
10081{_}2650{_}"I've got a knife," said Harris, "but I am afraid I wouldn't know what to do with it should a shark get after me."
10081{_}2651{_}The three became silent, saving all their strength for swimming.
10081{_}2652{_}An hour later they had drawn close to the vessel.
10081{_}2653{_}"It's a German all right," said Jack, regretfully.
10081{_}2654{_}"Any port in a storm," said Harris.
10081{_}2655{_}"That talk of shark a while back made me feel sort of squeamish.
10081{_}2656{_}I want to get out of this water."
10081{_}2657{_}They continued to swim toward the ship.
10081{_}2658{_}"Wonder what's the matter on board?"
10081{_}2659{_}exclaimed Frank, suddenly.
10081{_}2660{_}They had approached close enough now to see men rushing hurriedly about the deck.
10081{_}2661{_}Hoarse commands carried across the water, though the words were unintelligible to the three swimmers at that distance.
10081{_}2662{_}"Something wrong," said Jack, quietly.
10081{_}2663{_}"That's what I call hard luck," declared Frank.
10081{_}2664{_}"Here we think we have reached a place of safety and something goes wrong."
10081{_}2665{_}"Don't cry till you're hurt, youngster," said Harris, quietly.
10081{_}2666{_}"The ship is there and we're pretty close to it.
10081{_}2667{_}Those fellows aboard, German or English, are bound to lend us a hand."
10081{_}2668{_}"I'm not so sure about that," declared Frank.
10081{_}2669{_}"Well, I am," said Harris.
10081{_}2670{_}"The German sailor is all right.
10081{_}2671{_}It's the German officer who makes all the trouble.
10081{_}2672{_}They'll help us if they can."
10081{_}2673{_}The three swimmers were a short distance from the ship now.
10081{_}2674{_}Jack raised his voice in a shout.
10081{_}2675{_}"Help!"
10081{_}2676{_}he cried in German.
10081{_}2677{_}There was no move aboard the German vessel to indicate that the lad's cry had been heard.
10081{_}2678{_}"Told you so," said Frank.
10081{_}2679{_}"Don't cry too soon, youngster," said Harris.
10081{_}2680{_}"We'll try it again, and all yell together."
10081{_}2681{_}They did and this time their cries were heard.
10081{_}2682{_}Several men aboard the German vessel stopped their rushing about and gazed across the sea in the direction of the swimmers.
10081{_}2683{_}One man produced a glass and levelled it in their direction.
10081{_}2684{_}Then he turned to the others and they could be seen to gesticulate excitedly.
10081{_}2685{_}"One wants to save us and the others don't," declared Frank.
10081{_}2686{_}For some moments the men continued to argue.
10081{_}2687{_}One shook his finger in the faces of the others and pointed in the direction of the swimmers.
10081{_}2688{_}"You're all right," declared Frank, speaking of the one man.
10081{_}2689{_}"Wish I were there to lend you a hand.
10081{_}2690{_}But I'm afraid the others are too much for you."
10081{_}2691{_}At this juncture the man who opposed the others produced a revolver and made an angry gesture.
10081{_}2692{_}He was ordering the others to the aid of the three friends in the water.
10081{_}2693{_}"By Jove!"
10081{_}2694{_}said Harris.
10081{_}2695{_}"He's all right.
10081{_}2696{_}I'd like to be able to do him a good turn."
10081{_}2697{_}And the chance was to come sooner than he expected.
10081{_}2698{_}Apparently the men aboard the German vessel had decided to obey the order of the man who would save the three swimmers.
10081{_}2699{_}A boat was lowered over the side.
10081{_}2700{_}Three men stood ready to leap into it.
10081{_}2701{_}The hopes of the three friends in the water rose high; but they were shattered a moment later in a sudden and unexpected manner.
10081{_}2702{_}A dull rumbling roar came suddenly across the water.
10081{_}2703{_}Instantly all became confusion aboard the German vessel.
10081{_}2704{_}Officers shouted hoarse commands and struck out with the flat of their swords as members of the crew rushed for the rails.
10081{_}2705{_}"An explosion!"
10081{_}2706{_}cried Frank.
10081{_}2707{_}"Swim back quickly."
10081{_}2708{_}The others understood the significance of that strange rumbling aboard the German vessel as quickly as Frank, and turning rapidly, they struck out as fast as they could.
10081{_}2709{_}An explosion such as that dull roar indicated could have but one result and the lads knew it.
10081{_}2710{_}Evidently there had been a fire on board--that accounted for the strange activities of the men on the ship--and the flames had reached the vessel's magazine.
10081{_}2711{_}A second and a louder roar came now.
10081{_}2712{_}Men jumped into the sea by the scores and struck out vigorously that they might not be pulled under by the suction when the ship sank.
10081{_}2713{_}Then there came an explosion even louder than the rest.
10081{_}2714{_}The great ship parted in the middle as though cut by a knife.
10081{_}2715{_}A huge tongue of flame shot high in the air.
10081{_}2716{_}Hoarse cries from aboard, screams and frightful yells.
10081{_}2717{_}Split in twain, the vessel settled fore and aft.
10081{_}2718{_}A second huge tongue of flame leaped into the sky; and then the vessel disappeared beneath the sea.
10081{_}2719{_}Giant waves leaped in the direction taken by Jack, Frank and Harris.
10081{_}2720{_}The sea churned angrily about them and the three had all they could do to keep their heads above water.
10081{_}2721{_}Then the water calmed down.
10081{_}2722{_}Frank looked around and there, not fifty feet away, rolling gently on the waves, was the small boat so recently lowered over the side of the German vessel.
10081{_}2723{_}With a cry to the others to follow him, Frank turned about and headed for the boat with powerful strokes.
10081{_}2724{_}CHAPTER XX  FRIENDS AND FOES   There was reason for Frank's haste.
10081{_}2725{_}Swimming close together and bearing down upon the boat from the opposite direction--almost as close from their side as Frank was from his--four German sailors were racing.
10081{_}2726{_}They espied Frank and his friends at almost the same moment Frank saw them.
10081{_}2727{_}One uttered a cry and the others redoubled their efforts to beat Frank to the boat.
10081{_}2728{_}Jack and Harris took in the situation quickly.
10081{_}2729{_}It was then that Jack exerted himself to the utmost.
10081{_}2730{_}His great, powerful strokes sent him skimming through the water as lightly as a denizen of the deep.
10081{_}2731{_}A dozen strokes and he had passed Frank.
10081{_}2732{_}A few more only, it seemed, and he laid hold of the boat and drew himself aboard.
10081{_}2733{_}Standing erect he looked around quickly.
10081{_}2734{_}Then, stepping forward, he picked up an oar.
10081{_}2735{_}He moved to the side of the boat where the Germans were approaching and raised the oar aloft.
10081{_}2736{_}"Keep off there!"
10081{_}2737{_}he cried.
10081{_}2738{_}The Germans uttered exclamations of alarm; but they came closer.
10081{_}2739{_}"Keep back!"
10081{_}2740{_}cried Jack, again.
10081{_}2741{_}"But you won't let us drown!"
10081{_}2742{_}exclaimed one of the enemy.
10081{_}2743{_}"You stay there until my friends get aboard.
10081{_}2744{_}Then I'll see what I can do for you," replied Jack.
10081{_}2745{_}With this the Germans were forced to be content; for they realized that Jack held the upper hand.
10081{_}2746{_}It would be impossible for them to climb aboard while the lad stood there brandishing that oar.
10081{_}2747{_}Frank laid hold of the boat a moment later and clambered over the side.
10081{_}2748{_}Harris was close beside him.
10081{_}2749{_}Jack called a consultation.
10081{_}2750{_}"There is plenty of room for those fellows in here," he said, "but-- shall we let them in?"
10081{_}2751{_}"We can't see them drown," said Frank.
10081{_}2752{_}"Still, there is no telling how long we shall be here.
10081{_}2753{_}Is there sufficient water and food to go around?"
10081{_}2754{_}"I'll have a look," said Harris.
10081{_}2755{_}"Enough for seven of us for about one drink apiece," he said, after an exploration.
10081{_}2756{_}"There is no food."
10081{_}2757{_}"Well, what shall we do?"
10081{_}2758{_}said Jack.
10081{_}2759{_}"Let them come aboard," said Frank.
10081{_}2760{_}"We can't see them perish without raising a hand to help them."
10081{_}2761{_}"And yet they would not have helped us a short time ago," said Jack.
10081{_}2762{_}"One man would have helped us," said Harris.
10081{_}2763{_}"Perhaps he is one of these."
10081{_}2764{_}"No, he's not," said Jack.
10081{_}2765{_}"I would know him in a moment if I saw him.
10081{_}2766{_}I obtained a good look at his face."
10081{_}2767{_}"Let them in anyhow," said Harris.
10081{_}2768{_}"All right," said Jack.
10081{_}2769{_}He called to the men in the water.
10081{_}2770{_}"You fellows climb aboard here, one at a time; and when you get in, remember you are our prisoners.
10081{_}2771{_}Any foolishness and we'll pitch you back again."
10081{_}2772{_}The Germans offered no protest and climbed into the boat one at a time.
10081{_}2773{_}"Sit in the back, there," said Jack.
10081{_}2774{_}The men obeyed.
10081{_}2775{_}"Now," said Jack, "I'll tell you where we stand.
10081{_}2776{_}Water is scarce and there is no food.
10081{_}2777{_}We shall have to make for shore immediately.
10081{_}2778{_}I'm in command of this boat and you will have to obey me.
10081{_}2779{_}Get out the oars and row as I tell you."
10081{_}2780{_}The Germans grumbled a bit but they obeyed.
10081{_}2781{_}"No time to waste," said Jack, briefly.
10081{_}2782{_}"We'll head south."
10081{_}2783{_}He gave the necessary directions and the boat moved off.
10081{_}2784{_}"Help!"
10081{_}2785{_}came a sudden cry from the water.
10081{_}2786{_}Jack looked in the direction of this sound.
10081{_}2787{_}A single head came toward them, swimming weakly.
10081{_}2788{_}"Ship your oars, men," said Jack.
10081{_}2789{_}There came a grumble from one of the Germans.
10081{_}2790{_}"There is no more room," he declared.
10081{_}2791{_}"No," agreed a second.
10081{_}2792{_}"There is not enough water now.
10081{_}2793{_}Why should we let another man in the boat?"
10081{_}2794{_}"Stop that!"
10081{_}2795{_}said Jack, sharply.
10081{_}2796{_}"Cease rowing!"
10081{_}2797{_}The men made no move to obey.
10081{_}2798{_}Jack stood up in the boat and stepped forward.
10081{_}2799{_}"Did you hear me?"
10081{_}2800{_}he said quietly, though it was plain to Frank that he was very angry.
10081{_}2801{_}"Cease rowing!"
10081{_}2802{_}"But----" began the nearest German.
10081{_}2803{_}Jack wasted no further time in words.
10081{_}2804{_}His left arm shot out and he grasped the nearest German by the coat.
10081{_}2805{_}Raising him quickly to his feet, he struck him heavily with his right fist and then released his hold.
10081{_}2806{_}The man dropped to the bottom of the boat and lay still.
10081{_}2807{_}"Any more?"
10081{_}2808{_}asked Jack.
10081{_}2809{_}"Cease rowing!"
10081{_}2810{_}The remaining three Germans shipped their oars without a word, although each bestowed an evil glance upon the lad.
10081{_}2811{_}Frank, catching the look in their eyes, muttered to himself:  "They'll bear watching."
10081{_}2812{_}"Harris," said Jack.
10081{_}2813{_}"That man in the water is the one who would have saved us a short time ago.
10081{_}2814{_}He seems to be weak.
10081{_}2815{_}Slip over the side and lend him a hand, will you?"
10081{_}2816{_}Harris did so without question and a moment or two later the German tumbled into the boat, where he lay panting, blood streaming from an open wound in his forehead.
10081{_}2817{_}Harris climbed back in the boat.
10081{_}2818{_}"Bandage him up as well as you can and give him a few drops of that water," said Jack.
10081{_}2819{_}For his part, Jack stooped over the German soldier he had so recently knocked unconscious and raised him to a sitting posture.
10081{_}2820{_}Reaching over the side of the boat the lad wet his handkerchief and applied it to the German's head.
10081{_}2821{_}Soon the man recovered consciousness.
10081{_}2822{_}"A drop of water here, too," said Jack, quietly.
10081{_}2823{_}"Say," said Harris.
10081{_}2824{_}"This water is precious scarce.
10081{_}2825{_}We'll need it ourselves."
10081{_}2826{_}"But this man must have a little," said Jack.
10081{_}2827{_}"Pass it along."
10081{_}2828{_}Harris did not protest further and Jack allowed the German soldier to moisten his tongue.
10081{_}2829{_}"Now get back to your oars," the lad commanded.
10081{_}2830{_}The German did as commanded and soon the little boat was leaping lightly over the waves.
10081{_}2831{_}"Take the helm, Frank," said Jack.
10081{_}2832{_}Frank relieved Harris, who had been performing this duty.
10081{_}2833{_}"Got your pocket compass, Frank?"
10081{_}2834{_}asked Jack.
10081{_}2835{_}"Yes."
10081{_}2836{_}"Keep your course due south, then."
10081{_}2837{_}"All right, sir," said Frank, with a smile.
10081{_}2838{_}"Harris," said Jack, "I want you to stand guard over these sailors for a few minutes.
10081{_}2839{_}I want to have a talk with our latest arrival.
10081{_}2840{_}I'll be with you in a few minutes."
10081{_}2841{_}Harris stepped forward.
10081{_}2842{_}"Ought to have a gun, I suppose," he said.
10081{_}2843{_}"I guess not," said Jack.
10081{_}2844{_}"You and I together should be able to hold these fellows in check."
10081{_}2845{_}"Sure; unless they hit us over the head with an oar when we're not looking."
10081{_}2846{_}"But one of us must always be looking," said Jack, quietly.
10081{_}2847{_}"Well, that's not a bad idea.
10081{_}2848{_}I'll keep my eyes open."
10081{_}2849{_}Jack moved to the side of the German who had been the last to get into the boat.
10081{_}2850{_}His wound had been bound up as well as possible under the circumstances and he sat quietly, looking out over the water.
10081{_}2851{_}"What vessel was that?"
10081{_}2852{_}asked Jack.
10081{_}2853{_}"_Hanover_" was the reply.
10081{_}2854{_}"What was the trouble?"
10081{_}2855{_}"Shot pierced our boiler room in the battle.
10081{_}2856{_}Returning, we were lost from the main fleet in the fog.
10081{_}2857{_}Our wireless wouldn't work.
10081{_}2858{_}Fire broke out and we were unable to check the flames.
10081{_}2859{_}When they reached the magazine she exploded."
10081{_}2860{_}"I see," said Jack.
10081{_}2861{_}"It's fortunate you weren't drawn under with the ship."
10081{_}2862{_}"I was," said the German, briefly.
10081{_}2863{_}"What?"
10081{_}2864{_}exclaimed Jack.
10081{_}2865{_}"Yes.
10081{_}2866{_}I was drawn under.
10081{_}2867{_}I thought I was done for.
10081{_}2868{_}But, under the surface of the sea there was a second explosion.
10081{_}2869{_}I felt myself flying up through the water and then I shot into the air.
10081{_}2870{_}When I came down I was not far from your boat.
10081{_}2871{_}I called for help."
10081{_}2872{_}"By Jove!
10081{_}2873{_}you have had an experience few can boast of," said Jack.
10081{_}2874{_}"I wouldn't care to go through it."
10081{_}2875{_}"Nor I--again," said the German.
10081{_}2876{_}"Now," said Jack, "perhaps you can tell me the nearest way to shore."
10081{_}2877{_}The German considered.
10081{_}2878{_}"I am not a navigator," he said, "I was only a minor officer aboard the _Hanover_.
10081{_}2879{_}But I heard the captain say we were almost 100 miles from the nearest coast line.
10081{_}2880{_}I am afraid you will not be able to make it in this boat, if your water is as scarce as you say."
10081{_}2881{_}"By Jove!"
10081{_}2882{_}said Jack, "we've got to make it.
10081{_}2883{_}We don't want to drown out here."
10081{_}2884{_}"It's not always what we like," said the German officer, sententiously.
10081{_}2885{_}"That's true enough," agreed Jack, "but I have a feeling I was not born to be drowned.
10081{_}2886{_}We'll find a way out."
10081{_}2887{_}"I hope so.
10081{_}2888{_}However, should you go ashore directly south of here you would be within German lines and you would be made a prisoner."
10081{_}2889{_}"Can't help that," said Jack.
10081{_}2890{_}"I'd much rather be a live prisoner than a dead sailor."
10081{_}2891{_}The German smiled in spite of his wound, which, it was plain to all, was giving him great pain.
10081{_}2892{_}"Of course," he said, "there is always the possibility of a passing ship."
10081{_}2893{_}"That's what we thought before," said Jack.
10081{_}2894{_}"When we saw your vessel we thought we were safe.
10081{_}2895{_}But you see how it turned out."
10081{_}2896{_}"Well, you'll just have to select a course and stick to it," said the German.
10081{_}2897{_}"By the way, these men of mine.
10081{_}2898{_}You are likely to have trouble with them.
10081{_}2899{_}In our present situation I do not consider that we are enemies, so if the worst comes you may count on me to help you."
10081{_}2900{_}"Thanks," said Jack.
10081{_}2901{_}"I shall remember that."
10081{_}2902{_}And the trouble was to come sooner than could have been expected.
10081{_}2903{_}One of the German soldiers suddenly laid down his oars.
10081{_}2904{_}"I want a drink!"
10081{_}2905{_}he exclaimed.
10081{_}2906{_}"I'll row no more until I have a drink!"
10081{_}2907{_}CHAPTER XXI  A FIGHT FOR A BOAT   As by a prearranged signal, all four of the Germans threw down their oars and jumped to their feet.
10081{_}2908{_}Harris, at that moment, in spite of Jack's warning, had been gazing across the sea absolutely unconscious of his surroundings.
10081{_}2909{_}He was lost in thought.
10081{_}2910{_}Frank, at the helm, uttered a cry of warning even as the closest German leaped for Harris and the latter wheeled quickly.
10081{_}2911{_}He dodged just as the man struck out with a knife he had drawn.
10081{_}2912{_}"Want to cut me up, do you?"
10081{_}2913{_}muttered Harris.
10081{_}2914{_}In spite of the wabbling of the boat he fell into an attitude of defense--the old fighting form that had won for him the championship of the British navy in the squared circle.
10081{_}2915{_}He didn't advance, for he wasn't certain of his footing, the boat pitched so, but he felt fully able to take care of himself.
10081{_}2916{_}It was characteristic of him that he made no cry for help.
10081{_}2917{_}He knew that Jack must have heard Frank's cry of warning.
10081{_}2918{_}He knew that he would get all the assistance it was in Jack's power to give; and he felt that if Jack were unable for any reason to aid him he must, nevertheless, give a good account of himself.
10081{_}2919{_}When Harris evaded the first blow, the German, caught off his balance, pitched forward against him.
10081{_}2920{_}Harris was almost toppled over, but he threw his left arm around the man's neck and aimed a vicious blow at him with his right fist.
10081{_}2921{_}The German's knife arm, because of Harris' hold, dangled helpless at his side.
10081{_}2922{_}In vain he sought to get it in position where he could drive the point into Harris' body.
10081{_}2923{_}Harris realized the man's intention.
10081{_}2924{_}With a sudden move, he pushed the German from him and struck out as he did so.
10081{_}2925{_}The man staggered back, reeled unsteadily and toppled over the side of the boat with a cry.
10081{_}2926{_}The three other Germans rushed Harris at that moment.
10081{_}2927{_}This time the British sailor was not caught off his guard, and he held the men at arm's length for several seconds.
10081{_}2928{_}Meanwhile, Jack had leaped forward, crying to Frank as he did so:  "Keep the helm, Frank!
10081{_}2929{_}We don't want the boat overturned."
10081{_}2930{_}Frank obeyed, much as he would have liked to join in the fight.
10081{_}2931{_}Jack reached Harris' side and together the two faced the three Germans.
10081{_}2932{_}"We've got them, now," said Harris, quietly.
10081{_}2933{_}"Men," said Jack, quietly, "unless you return to your oars immediately, we shall be forced to throw you overboard."
10081{_}2934{_}There was a snarl from the three men.
10081{_}2935{_}Suddenly one dropped to his knees and seized Harris by the legs.
10081{_}2936{_}Caught off his guard, the latter fell to the bottom of the boat and the others leaped on him.
10081{_}2937{_}A knife flashed in the hand of one.
10081{_}2938{_}With a cry, Jack stooped down quickly and seized the man's wrist even as the point of the weapon would have been buried in Harris' back.
10081{_}2939{_}The lad twisted sharply and the knife went flying into the sea.
10081{_}2940{_}"You would, would you!"
10081{_}2941{_}cried Jack.
10081{_}2942{_}He jerked the man to his feet, planted two hard blows on his chin, and as the man reeled forward clipped him once more.
10081{_}2943{_}One, two, three backward steps the man took and then pitched over the side of the boat.
10081{_}2944{_}"Two gone!"
10081{_}2945{_}exclaimed Jack.
10081{_}2946{_}But he was wrong.
10081{_}2947{_}For the first man who had been knocked into the sea had been revived by the shock of the cold water.
10081{_}2948{_}Swimming around the boat unobserved, he had come up behind Frank and now reached up and grabbed Frank by the coat.
10081{_}2949{_}With a cry of alarm, the lad toppled into the water.
10081{_}2950{_}Jack heard his friend's cry.
10081{_}2951{_}Quickly he took in the situation.
10081{_}2952{_}Harris had regained his feet and seemed capable of disposing of the two remaining Germans.
10081{_}2953{_}With a cry to Harris, Jack leaped over the side.
10081{_}2954{_}Some distance away he saw Frank struggling with the German who had pulled him from the boat and he swam quickly in that direction.
10081{_}2955{_}"I'm coming, Frank!"
10081{_}2956{_}he called.
10081{_}2957{_}"Hang on to him."
10081{_}2958{_}Frank was doing his best, but he had been taken by surprise and the advantage was with his opponent.
10081{_}2959{_}The German's hand closed about the lad's throat and he was slowly choking him.
10081{_}2960{_}Even as Jack came abreast of the struggling figures, Frank threw up his hands and the two disappeared from sight.
10081{_}2961{_}Jack, greatly alarmed, dived after them.
10081{_}2962{_}Below the surface of the water his hands encountered the struggling figures.
10081{_}2963{_}He seized the first his hand came in contact with and struck upward.
10081{_}2964{_}Upon the surface again, he found that he had seized hold of Frank.
10081{_}2965{_}Keeping his fingers clenched tightly in Frank's coat--that the lad might not be drawn under again Jack aimed carefully at the face of the German, which now was close to him, and struck out with all his strength.
10081{_}2966{_}Instantly, the hand on Frank's throat relaxed and the German sank from sight.
10081{_}2967{_}By the force of the impact as the blow landed Jack knew that the German would trouble them no more.
10081{_}2968{_}Supporting Frank with his left arm, he struck out for the boat with his right.
10081{_}2969{_}The German officer leaned over the side and lent a hand in dragging Frank's limp body over the side.
10081{_}2970{_}Jack clambered over after him.
10081{_}2971{_}Then he took a view of the part of the boat where Harris battled with two of the enemy.
10081{_}2972{_}Both of the latter wielded knives and it was plain to Jack that Harris hesitated to come to close quarters with them, as he had no assistance at hand; for he realized that, should he be overcome, the men would have little trouble of disposing of Frank and Jack, as they tried to climb back in the boat.
10081{_}2973{_}But now that Jack was able to come to his assistance again, Harris made ready for a spring.
10081{_}2974{_}Jack saw this move and called:  "Wait a minute, Harris!"
10081{_}2975{_}Harris stayed his spring and Jack again advanced to his side.
10081{_}2976{_}Jack's face was white and his clothing was dripping water.
10081{_}2977{_}He was very angry and his fingers clenched and unclenched.
10081{_}2978{_}"You men," he said in a cold voice, "were given a chance for your lives the same as the rest of us.
10081{_}2979{_}Now you will either throw down those knives or die."
10081{_}2980{_}One made as if to obey, but the other stopped him.
10081{_}2981{_}"Wait!"
10081{_}2982{_}he cried.
10081{_}2983{_}"He wants us to throw down our knives so they can overpower us."
10081{_}2984{_}To the other this seemed good reasoning.
10081{_}2985{_}Both Germans, still wielding their weapons, drew backward slowly.
10081{_}2986{_}Jack and Harris advanced as slowly after them.
10081{_}2987{_}"Drop them!"
10081{_}2988{_}cried Jack, again.
10081{_}2989{_}Suddenly one of the Germans sprang forward and aimed a vicious blow at Jack with his knife.
10081{_}2990{_}The move had been so unexpected, retreating as the men had been, that Jack was almost caught off his guard.
10081{_}2991{_}He sidestepped quickly, however, and avoided the knife.
10081{_}2992{_}But in leaping aside he had jostled Harris, who, dodging a blow aimed by the second German, now was thrown off his balance.
