10081{_}4116{_}Frank uttered a cry of consternation:  "The three of clubs!"
10081{_}4117{_}"Looks like I was the fellow to stay, all right," said Jack, smiling slightly.
10081{_}4118{_}"And this time," said Frank, "you may not be as fortunate as upon the day you remained behind and faced death on the submarine."
10081{_}4119{_}Jack shrugged.
10081{_}4120{_}"Can't be helped," he said quietly.
10081{_}4121{_}Now Harris advanced and cut the cards quickly.
10081{_}4122{_}As he picked up the upper half of the deck, he turned his shoulder slightly so that the others, for the moment, might not see what he had cut.
10081{_}4123{_}He glanced at the bottom card.
10081{_}4124{_}It was the six of diamonds.
10081{_}4125{_}Deftly, Harris shuffled the cards with his hands.
10081{_}4126{_}Adept in the art of trickery, though the others did not know it, he had placed the cards in such position that he knew almost identically where the high and low cards were.
10081{_}4127{_}Like a flash his hand passed across the bottom of the deck and when it was withdrawn the six of diamonds had disappeared.
10081{_}4128{_}Then he turned to the others and exposed:  The two spot of spades!
10081{_}4129{_}"I lose," he said quietly.
10081{_}4130{_}Harris' movements had been so quick that they had not been perceived by the others.
10081{_}4131{_}Jack was the first to extend a hand.
10081{_}4132{_}"I'm sorry," the lad said quietly.
10081{_}4133{_}"I was in hopes that it would be me."
10081{_}4134{_}As he shook hands with the others, Harris kept his left hand behind him; for in it reposed the card he had palmed--the six of diamonds, which would have allowed him to go with the others and would have put Jack in his place.
10081{_}4135{_}As he turned, Harris slipped the card quickly into his pocket, that it might not be accidentally seen.
10081{_}4136{_}Then, he knew, he was safe.
10081{_}4137{_}Jack picked up the deck.
10081{_}4138{_}"I shall keep these, Harris," he said, "that I may always remember a brave man."
10081{_}4139{_}All this time the thundering on the door of the companionway had continued.
10081{_}4140{_}"Come," said von Ludwig, "we must delay no longer.
10081{_}4141{_}Already it is growing light."
10081{_}4142{_}He hastened along the deck to where the high-powered motor boat lay covered with a tarpaulin.
10081{_}4143{_}Quickly the little craft was lowered over the side, von Ludwig first inspecting it.
10081{_}4144{_}"Plenty of water and provisions," he said quietly.
10081{_}4145{_}He turned to Harris.
10081{_}4146{_}"It is time to say goodbye," he said quietly.
10081{_}4147{_}"You are a brave man.
10081{_}4148{_}This gallant action shall be known to the world."
10081{_}4149{_}"Goodbye, sir," said Harris, quietly.
10081{_}4150{_}"Remember," said von Ludwig, "there is always a chance that you may escape.
10081{_}4151{_}If it comes, make the most of it.
10081{_}4152{_}Goodbye."
10081{_}4153{_}He pressed Harris' hand and passed over the side of the vessel.
10081{_}4154{_}As Frank and Jack shook hands with Harris, the latter squeezed Harris' hand affectionately.
10081{_}4155{_}The latter smiled.
10081{_}4156{_}"I had promised myself another bout with you some day," he said.
10081{_}4157{_}"My only regret is that it is not possible now."
10081{_}4158{_}A moment more Jack was in the motor boat and it moved away.
10081{_}4159{_}Harris drew his revolvers and mounted guard over the companionway, the door of which now had begun to splinter.
10081{_}4160{_}"An hour is what you needed," he said quietly.
10081{_}4161{_}"You'll get it!"
10081{_}4162{_}CHAPTER XXIX  A CHAMPION PASSES   Harris laid one of his revolvers on the deck, reached in his pocket and produced the six of diamonds.
10081{_}4163{_}He looked at it closely in the half darkness and a smile passed over his face.
10081{_}4164{_}"I suppose I'm a fool," he muttered to himself, "but someway I couldn't help it.
10081{_}4165{_}I was afraid Jack would cut the low card.
10081{_}4166{_}I wouldn't have done it for one of the others, but Jack, well, he's a boy after my own heart."
10081{_}4167{_}Harris replaced the card in his pocket; then thought better of his action, drew it forth again and sent it spinning off across the sea.
10081{_}4168{_}"There," he said quietly, "goes all evidence that I cheated."
10081{_}4169{_}He picked up the revolver he had laid on the deck and moved a short distance from the companionway.
10081{_}4170{_}There was an extra violent crash and it seemed that the door must burst open.
10081{_}4171{_}"Another one like that will do the work," said Harris, calmly.
10081{_}4172{_}He took up what he considered a strategic position and produced his watch.
10081{_}4173{_}This he lay on the deck and sat down beside it.
10081{_}4174{_}"May as well be comfortable," he remarked.
10081{_}4175{_}Again there was a crash and the door of the companionway burst open.
10081{_}4176{_}A German head appeared.
10081{_}4177{_}"Crack!"
10081{_}4178{_}Harris had fired without moving from his sitting posture.
10081{_}4179{_}The German head disappeared and there was a cry of alarm from below.
10081{_}4180{_}"One down, I guess," said Harris, quietly, to himself.
10081{_}4181{_}For some moments there was silence, broken occasionally, however, by the dull sound of voices from below.
10081{_}4182{_}"Talking it over, eh?"
10081{_}4183{_}muttered Harris.
10081{_}4184{_}"Well, I'll still be here when you try again."
10081{_}4185{_}It was perhaps fifteen minutes later that a cap appeared in the opening.
10081{_}4186{_}Again Harris fired.
10081{_}4187{_}The cap did not disappear and Harris fired twice more quickly.
10081{_}4188{_}The cap disappeared.
10081{_}4189{_}"Guess I got another one," said Harris.
10081{_}4190{_}Twice more within the next fifteen minutes this happened.
10081{_}4191{_}"That should be four, if I have counted correctly," said Harris; "and I've still four cartridges left.
10081{_}4192{_}I won't have to reload yet."
10081{_}4193{_}He felt in his pocket and then uttered an exclamation of alarm.
10081{_}4194{_}"No more bullets.
10081{_}4195{_}I'll have to make these four count for the next two."
10081{_}4196{_}Nothing appeared in the doorway again for ten minutes more and then Harris fired again.
10081{_}4197{_}Fifteen minutes later the same thing happened and Harris, making sure that this was the last of the enemy, emptied his revolver at it.
10081{_}4198{_}Then he got to his feet and put his watch in his pocket.
10081{_}4199{_}"Guess that settles it," he said.
10081{_}4200{_}"Now I'll look around for a boat.
10081{_}4201{_}I didn't know it was going to be as easy as all that.
10081{_}4202{_}If I had I would have had the others wait for me."
10081{_}4203{_}He moved toward the companionway, and as he did so, a bullet whistled by his ear.
10081{_}4204{_}Harris stepped back in surprise; and in that moment the solution came to him.
10081{_}4205{_}"By Jove!
10081{_}4206{_}They've fooled me," he muttered.
10081{_}4207{_}"They poked their caps up and I shot them full of holes.
10081{_}4208{_}However, they don't know yet that I'm out of bullets."
10081{_}4209{_}A few moments later a cap again appeared in the opening.
10081{_}4210{_}Harris had no bullets to fire at it.
10081{_}4211{_}"They'll discover my predicament in a moment or so, though," he told himself.
10081{_}4212{_}He pulled his watch from his pocket and glanced at it.
10081{_}4213{_}"An hour," he said.
10081{_}4214{_}"They have had time enough.
10081{_}4215{_}However, I'll just see the thing through."
10081{_}4216{_}As he spoke it grew light.
10081{_}4217{_}Harris looked off across the sea.
10081{_}4218{_}There, so far away that it appeared but a speck upon the water, he saw what he took to be the motor boat bearing his friends to safety.
10081{_}4219{_}He waved his cap.
10081{_}4220{_}"Good luck!"
10081{_}4221{_}he said quietly.
10081{_}4222{_}Now a German head appeared in the door of the companionway.
10081{_}4223{_}It was not a cap this time.
10081{_}4224{_}Harris saw it, and drawing back his arm, hurled one of his revolvers swiftly.
10081{_}4225{_}His aim was true and the weapon struck the German squarely in the face.
10081{_}4226{_}With a scream of pain the man fell back into the arms of his companions.
10081{_}4227{_}But Harris' action had told his enemies that he had no more bullets, and seeing that they had but one man to contend with, the Germans sprang from their shelter and leaped for him.
10081{_}4228{_}Harris clubbed his remaining revolver, and with his back to the pilot house, where he had retreated, awaited the approach of the four foes.
10081{_}4229{_}"You're going to have the fight of your lives," he said grimly.
10081{_}4230{_}A German sprang.
10081{_}4231{_}Harris' arm rose and fell and there was one German less to contend with.
10081{_}4232{_}But before Harris could raise his arm again, the other three had closed in upon him.
10081{_}4233{_}Harris felt himself borne back.
10081{_}4234{_}The former pugilistic champion of the British navy cast all ring ethics to the winds.
10081{_}4235{_}He struck, kicked and clawed and sought to wreak what damage he could upon his enemies without regard for the niceties of fighting.
10081{_}4236{_}He knew that they would do the same to him.
10081{_}4237{_}So great had been the force of the shock of the three Germans--all that were now left of the original twelve--that Harris was borne to the deck.
10081{_}4238{_}His revolver hand struck the floor with great force and the weapon was sent spinning from his grasp.
10081{_}4239{_}With a mighty effort, he hurled the three men from him and leaped to his feet.
10081{_}4240{_}The Germans also arose.
10081{_}4241{_}Harris did not wait for them to resume the offensive.
10081{_}4242{_}With head lowered he charged.
10081{_}4243{_}Nimbly the foe skipped to either side and Harris felt a keen pain in his right side.
10081{_}4244{_}One of the foe had drawn a knife and stabbed as Harris rushed by.
10081{_}4245{_}Whirling quickly, Harris again sprang forward.
10081{_}4246{_}One man did not leap out of his way quickly enough, and Harris' hands found his throat.
10081{_}4247{_}The man gave a screech as Harris' hands squeezed.
10081{_}4248{_}The Englishman raised his enemy bodily from the deck, flung him squarely in the faces of the other two, and followed after the human catapult.
10081{_}4249{_}The foremost German dodged and seized Harris by the legs.
10081{_}4250{_}Both went over in a heap, Harris on top.
10081{_}4251{_}Harris raised his right fist and would have brought it down on the German's face but for the fact that the second foe seized his arm in a fierce grasp.
10081{_}4252{_}At the same moment he struck with his knife.
10081{_}4253{_}The point penetrated Harris' right side and he felt himself growing faint.
10081{_}4254{_}Angrily, he shook the German from him and rose to his feet.
10081{_}4255{_}The man who had been underneath the Englishman also got quickly to his feet, and before Harris could turn, stabbed him in the back.
10081{_}4256{_}With a cry, Harris whirled on him and seized the knife arm.
10081{_}4257{_}He twisted sharply.
10081{_}4258{_}The German cried out in pain and sought to free himself.
10081{_}4259{_}But his effort was in vain.
10081{_}4260{_}With the grasp by the wrist, Harris swung the man in the air, and spinning on his heel, hurled him far across the deck, where the unconscious form struck with a crash; and at the same moment the other German struck again with his knife.
10081{_}4261{_}Harris staggered back.
10081{_}4262{_}Now the German who so recently had felt the effect of Harris' fingers in his throat, pulled himself from the deck and renewed the battle.
10081{_}4263{_}He advanced, crouching, and another knife gleamed in his hand.
10081{_}4264{_}It is possible that, had it not been for the effects of the knife wounds, Harris, in the end, would have overcome these foes, for he was a powerful man.
10081{_}4265{_}But when a man is bleeding from half a dozen wounds and faces two adversaries both armed with knives, he has little chance of ultimate victory.
10081{_}4266{_}Harris realized it; but he was not the man to beg for mercy.
10081{_}4267{_}Besides, so fierce had been his attacks and so great his execution, it is not probable that the Germans would have spared him anyhow.
10081{_}4268{_}They were insane with rage.
10081{_}4269{_}There were only two of them left now; and Harris told himself that their number would be fewer by one before they finished with him.
10081{_}4270{_}He leaned against the pilot house panting from his exertions.
10081{_}4271{_}"A great lot of fighters, you are," he taunted his enemies.
10081{_}4272{_}"Four of you attacked me with knives and you haven't done for me yet."
10081{_}4273{_}The Germans also were glad of a breathing spell.
10081{_}4274{_}Their faces reddened as Harris taunted them.
10081{_}4275{_}"We shall kill you yet," said one angrily.
10081{_}4276{_}"Don't be too sure," said Harris.
10081{_}4277{_}"I'm an Englishman, you know, and you have always been afraid of an Englishman."
10081{_}4278{_}At this the Germans uttered a cry of rage and sprang forward, their knives flashing aloft.
10081{_}4279{_}The first German missed his mark as Harris dodged beneath his arm and closed with him.
10081{_}4280{_}He uttered a cry for help.
10081{_}4281{_}"That's right, you coward!
10081{_}4282{_}You'll need it," said Harris.
10081{_}4283{_}He squeezed the man with all his might.
10081{_}4284{_}Out of the tail of his eye he caught the glint of the other German's knife as it descended.
10081{_}4285{_}Releasing his hold upon the one man, he stepped quickly backward.
10081{_}4286{_}But the knife caught him a glancing blow on the forehead, inflicting a deep wound.
10081{_}4287{_}For a moment Harris paused to shake the blood out of his eyes.
10081{_}4288{_}Then, with a smile playing across his features, he advanced; and as he advanced he said:  "You've done for me, the lot of you.
10081{_}4289{_}But I shall take you with me."
10081{_}4290{_}The Germans quailed at the look in his face; and as he moved forward swiftly they threw down their knives and turned to run.
10081{_}4291{_}But they had delayed too long.
10081{_}4292{_}Harris stretched both hands out straight before him.
10081{_}4293{_}One hand closed about the arm of the German to his right.
10081{_}4294{_}The other clutched the second man by the throat.
10081{_}4295{_}Harris pulled the man he held by the arm close; then released his grip, but before the German could stagger away, seized him, too, by the throat.
10081{_}4296{_}"Now I've got you," he said.
10081{_}4297{_}Blow after blow the Germans rained upon his face and shoulders, kicking out with their feet the while.
10081{_}4298{_}Harris paid no more attention to these than he would have to the taps of a child.
10081{_}4299{_}But the Englishman felt his strength waning fast.
10081{_}4300{_}It was with an effort that he staggered across the deck.
10081{_}4301{_}At the rail he paused for a moment, gathering his strength for a final effort.
10081{_}4302{_}Then, still holding a German by the throat with each hand, he leaped into the sea.
10081{_}4303{_}Once, twice, three times the three heads appeared on the surface and a spectator could have seen that Harris retained his grip.
10081{_}4304{_}Then the three sank from sight.
10081{_}4305{_}And so passed the former pugilistic champion of the British fleet, brave in death as he had been in life.
10081{_}4306{_}The waves washed over the spot where he had gone down.
10081{_}4307{_}CHAPTER XXX  THE UNKNOWN UNMASKS   With the coming of dawn the three figures in the little motor boat gazed back in the direction from whence they had come.
10081{_}4308{_}There they could still make out the distant shape of the _Bismarck_.
10081{_}4309{_}She rode quietly in the water, and there was nothing about her appearance to tell the three in the motor boat of the terrible struggle that was raging even at that moment.
10081{_}4310{_}"Poor Harris," said Jack.
10081{_}4311{_}"I hope that in some manner he is able to escape."
10081{_}4312{_}"Certainly I hope so, too," declared Frank.
10081{_}4313{_}"He's a brave man," said von Ludwig.
10081{_}4314{_}Jack drew the fateful deck of cards from his pocket.
10081{_}4315{_}"These," he said, "I shall keep."
10081{_}4316{_}He ran through the deck several times, playing with them.
10081{_}4317{_}Unconsciously he counted them.
10081{_}4318{_}There was something wrong.
10081{_}4319{_}Jack counted the cards again.
10081{_}4320{_}The result was the same.
10081{_}4321{_}"Sir!"
10081{_}4322{_}he called to von Ludwig.
10081{_}4323{_}"Well?"
10081{_}4324{_}"How did you chance to have this pack of cards?"
10081{_}4325{_}"I play solitaire considerably," was the reply.
10081{_}4326{_}"You couldn't have played solitaire with this deck," said Jack.
10081{_}4327{_}"Why not?"
10081{_}4328{_}"All the cards are not here.
10081{_}4329{_}There are but fifty-one."
10081{_}4330{_}"There were fifty-two when I put them in my pocket," said von Ludwig, "because I counted them."
10081{_}4331{_}Again Jack ran through the deck There were but fifty-one cards.
10081{_}4332{_}Suddenly the lad gave a start.
10081{_}4333{_}He spread the cards out in the bottom of the boat, making four piles all suits together.
10081{_}4334{_}He counted the hearts.
10081{_}4335{_}They were all there, thirteen of them.
10081{_}4336{_}He counted the clubs.
10081{_}4337{_}They were all there, too.
10081{_}4338{_}Next he counted the spades.
10081{_}4339{_}All were there.
10081{_}4340{_}Last he counted the diamonds.
10081{_}4341{_}There were but twelve.
10081{_}4342{_}Jack arranged them in order.
10081{_}4343{_}There was one card shy.
10081{_}4344{_}Jack found what it was a moment later.
10081{_}4345{_}There was no six of diamonds in the deck.
10081{_}4346{_}For some moments Jack sat silent, staring at the cards before him.
10081{_}4347{_}He had been struck with a great light.
10081{_}4348{_}"So!"
10081{_}4349{_}he said to himself at last, "Harris cheated."
10081{_}4350{_}"What's that?"
10081{_}4351{_}said Frank, who had heard Jack's muttered words, but had not caught their import.
10081{_}4352{_}"I said," replied Jack, slowly, "that Harris cheated."
10081{_}4353{_}Frank was surprised.
10081{_}4354{_}A moment later he said: "Well, even if he did, he lost anyhow."
10081{_}4355{_}"That's it," said Jack, quietly.
10081{_}4356{_}"He didn't lose."
10081{_}4357{_}"You mean----" exclaimed Frank, excitedly.
10081{_}4358{_}"Yes; I mean that I lost.
10081{_}4359{_}I should have been the one to stay."
10081{_}4360{_}"Impossible," said Frank.
10081{_}4361{_}"It's true," declared Jack.
10081{_}4362{_}"Von Ludwig here says the deck was a full deck.
10081{_}4363{_}It's shy a card now.
10081{_}4364{_}The six of diamonds is missing.
10081{_}4365{_}That is the card Harris cut first.
10081{_}4366{_}You remember he turned aside?"
10081{_}4367{_}"Yes, but----"  "That's when he slipped the six of diamonds out of sight and exposed the deuce of spades."
10081{_}4368{_}"What's all this talk about cards?"
10081{_}4369{_}asked von Ludwig, at this juncture.
10081{_}4370{_}Jack explained and for a few moments von Ludwig was lost in thought.
10081{_}4371{_}"You know," he said, finally, "I think more of that fellow every minute.
10081{_}4372{_}That's the one case I have ever heard of where a man cheated with honor."
10081{_}4373{_}There was silence aboard the little craft as it sped over the water, all three aboard keeping a close watch for the approach of a German vessel of some sort.
10081{_}4374{_}Von Ludwig referred to his chart occasionally, for he wished to steer as clear of mines as possible.
10081{_}4375{_}They might be deep in the water and they might be close to the surface.
10081{_}4376{_}There was no use taking chances.
10081{_}4377{_}And while the voyage continued the lads were to be treated to yet another surprise; but this surprise was to be a pleasure and would not bring heavy hearts, as had the discovery of the missing card.
10081{_}4378{_}"I wish," said Jack, suddenly, to von Ludwig, "that you would tell me who you really are.
10081{_}4379{_}I sit here and look at you and know I should be able to call your name.
10081{_}4380{_}But I can't do it and it makes it decidedly unpleasant."
10081{_}4381{_}Von Ludwig smiled.
10081{_}4382{_}"I should have thought you would know me in a minute in spite of my disguise," he said quietly.
10081{_}4383{_}"I am sure I should have known both of you no matter what pains you took to conceal your features."
10081{_}4384{_}"You're only making matters worse," said Frank.
10081{_}4385{_}"Come on now and tell us who you are."
10081{_}4386{_}Again von Ludwig smiled.
10081{_}4387{_}"I wonder if you can guess who I am when I say that I can tell you all about yourselves?"
10081{_}4388{_}he said.
10081{_}4389{_}"For instance, you, Jack.
10081{_}4390{_}You spent most of your life in a little African village.
10081{_}4391{_}And you, Frank, are an American who was shanghaied aboard a sailing vessel in Naples soon after the outbreak of the war."
10081{_}4392{_}"By Jove!"
10081{_}4393{_}said Jack.
10081{_}4394{_}"Outside of Frank here there is only one man who knows all that about me."
10081{_}4395{_}"And there is but a single man who knows as much of me," declared Frank.
10081{_}4396{_}"Can it be----"  For answer von Ludwig rose in his seat and stripped from his face the heavy German beard that had given him the true Teutonic expression, and there stood revealed before Jack and Frank none other than Lord Hastings, their erstwhile commander and good friend.
10081{_}4397{_}Frank gave a cry of delight and sprang forward at the imminent risk of upsetting the motor boat.
10081{_}4398{_}He seized Lord Hastings' hand and pressed it warmly.
10081{_}4399{_}The latter's greeting was no less affectionate.
10081{_}4400{_}Jack, not so given to demonstrations as his chum, also advanced and grasped Lord Hasting's hand.
10081{_}4401{_}"You don't know how glad I am to see you again, sir," the lad said quietly.
10081{_}4402{_}"It seems like an age since we saw you.
10081{_}4403{_}And to think that we didn't recognize you instantly."
10081{_}4404{_}"That's what seemed so funny to me," said Lord Hastings.
10081{_}4405{_}"When I first saw you aboard that German vessel I was fearful for a minute that you would recognize me and blurt it out right there."
10081{_}4406{_}"But what were you doing there, Lord Hastings?"
10081{_}4407{_}asked Frank.
10081{_}4408{_}"It's a long story," was the latter's reply, "but I guess now is as good a time as any to explain."
10081{_}4409{_}"I wish you would, sir," said Jack.
10081{_}4410{_}"Well," said Lord Hastings, "as you know, I told you when we parted that I had an important diplomatic duty to perform.
10081{_}4411{_}First, it carried me to Roumania, where, I may say, I was successful."
10081{_}4412{_}"You mean that Roumania has decided to cast in her fortunes with the Allies, sir?"
10081{_}4413{_}"Exactly.
10081{_}4414{_}She will take that step some time in August, though the exact date I am unable to say.
10081{_}4415{_}My mission there at an end, I was ordered to report to Berlin.
10081{_}4416{_}As you know, we still maintain a staff of correspondents in the German capital, although their identities are closely hidden."
10081{_}4417{_}Frank and Jack nodded, for they had known this some time before.
10081{_}4418{_}"Well," Lord Hastings continued, "in Berlin I was instructed to learn what Germany planned to do to offset the Roumanian menace, for she is sure to know of Roumanians decision by this time.
10081{_}4419{_}I had some trouble, but I succeeded at last."
10081{_}4420{_}"And what will she do, sir?"
10081{_}4421{_}asked Frank.
10081{_}4422{_}"That," was the reply, "I am unable to state at this minute.
10081{_}4423{_}It is a secret that I am guarding carefully and I cannot even tell you lads about it."
10081{_}4424{_}Frank and Jack asked no further questions along that line.
10081{_}4425{_}"But how came you aboard the German vessel, sir?"
10081{_}4426{_}Jack wanted to know.
10081{_}4427{_}Lord Hastings smiled.
10081{_}4428{_}"In Berlin," he said, "I was supposed to be a Roumanian officer, who had hopes of changing the attitude of that country.
10081{_}4429{_}The Kaiser wished to show me how foolish it would be for the little Balkan state to join the Allies, and for that reason, had me shown through the German naval fortifications.
10081{_}4430{_}That information, too, I am carrying back with me."
10081{_}4431{_}"But why didn't you tell us who you were in Bremen, sir?"
10081{_}4432{_}"I don't know.
10081{_}4433{_}At first I guess because I wanted to surprise you both when you did learn who I was."
10081{_}4434{_}"But you told us not to try and learn who you were."
10081{_}4435{_}"Well, that was for a good reason.
10081{_}4436{_}For, if you should have sought to pry, it might have aroused suspicions and there is no telling what would have happened."
10081{_}4437{_}"I see, sir," said Frank.
10081{_}4438{_}"But you almost lost us when you didn't get back in time."
10081{_}4439{_}"I know that now.
10081{_}4440{_}I wouldn't do the same thing again."
10081{_}4441{_}"And what are you going to do after you return to London, sir?"
10081{_}4442{_}Frank wanted to know.
10081{_}4443{_}Again Lord Hastings smiled.
10081{_}4444{_}"That's hard to tell," he replied.
10081{_}4445{_}"Still, I imagine it will not be very long before I feel a deck under my heels again."
10081{_}4446{_}"You mean you will leave the diplomatic service again, sir?"
10081{_}4447{_}asked Jack.
10081{_}4448{_}"I expect to.
10081{_}4449{_}The king promised me a new command before he despatched me to the Balkans.
10081{_}4450{_}But I do not know how long I shall be kept waiting."
10081{_}4451{_}"And when you get it, sir, will we go back with you?"
10081{_}4452{_}asked Frank.
10081{_}4453{_}"Why," was the reply, "I should have thought that by this time you would perhaps have changed your minds."
10081{_}4454{_}"Never, sir," declared Jack, positively.
10081{_}4455{_}"We would rather serve under you, sir."
10081{_}4456{_}"I'll see what can be done," Lord Hastings promised.
10081{_}4457{_}And with that the lads were forced to be content.
10081{_}4458{_}Still, they knew well enough that Lord Hastings would do what he could to have them with him again.
10081{_}4459{_}"The main thing now," said Lord Hastings, "is to dodge the enemy and get back to England."
10081{_}4460{_}"With you here, sir," said Frank, "I am sure we shall get back safely."
10081{_}4461{_}And Frank proved a good prophet.
10081{_}4462{_}All that day they made their way slowly through the North Sea.
10081{_}4463{_}Several times enemy ships were sighted, but, because the little motor boat lay so low in the water, the Germans did not see them.
10081{_}4464{_}With the coming of night, however, Lord Hastings increased the speed of the little craft.
10081{_}4465{_}He felt that they were now beyond the German mine fields and that if another vessel were encountered it probably would be British.
10081{_}4466{_}And this proved to be the case.
10081{_}4467{_}Along toward morning of the second day, a British cruiser bore down on them.
10081{_}4468{_}Soon all were aboard the vessel, which, when Lord Hastings informed the commander of the nature of the papers he carried, turned about and headed for London.
10081{_}4469{_}A day or two later, Frank and Jack again found themselves installed in the comfortable home of Lord Hastings, where they sat down to await what time might bring forth--confident, however, that it would not be long before they were upon active service under the command of their good friend, Lord Hastings.
